Proof from the Quranic Promise of Succession
Sanusi interprets a Quranic verse as a fulfilled prophecy regarding the Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses a Quranic promise to prove the truth of prophethood by identifying its fulfillment in the Companions.

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecy is evidence of truth.

Sanusi presents a Quranic verse that promises succession and security to believers. He argues that this promise was fulfilled specifically in the Companions, demonstrating that the Prophet's message was from Allah. Let's examine how he uses textual indicators to identify the referent and the historical context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully.
The passage quotes part of verse 24:55.
2
Identify the claim
Sanusi claims the verse refers to the Companions. Note the two pieces of evidence he provides.
Evidence: 'among you' and the fear-to-security change.
3
Understand the context
The Companions were fearful in early Islam. The promise of security was fulfilled historically.
This fulfillment demonstrates the truth of the prophecy.
4
Connect to prophethood
A fulfilled prophecy shows the Prophet's message is true, a key argument in proving prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ ﴾ ، والمراد بهمُ : الصحابة رضي الله تعالى عنهم ؛ بدليل قولِهِ : مِنكُم ، وبدليل قوله : ﴿ وَلَيُبَدِّلَنَّهُم مِّنْ بَعْدِ خَوْفِهِمْ أَمَنًا ﴾ [النور : ٥٥] ، وكانوا هم الخائفين في صدر الإسلام (۱) .
He will surely grant them succession in the land, and what is meant by them are the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, by evidence of His saying: 'among you', and by evidence of His saying: 'And He will surely change them, after their fear, to security' [An-Nur: 55], and they were the ones who were fearful in early Islam.
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the Quran. It cites the verse where Allah promises to grant succession to those who believe and do good deeds. Sanusi explains that the verse refers specifically to the Companions, as indicated by the phrase 'among you' and the subsequent description of replacing fear with security. The fulfillment of this promise to the fearful early Muslims demonstrates the truth of the Prophet's message.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف
الصحابة
الخوف
الأمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the promise of succession and security in 24:55 applies to all believers equally, without specific reference to the Companions.
Correction: Sanusi demonstrates through the phrase 'among you' and the historical context of fear that the verse specifically addresses the Companions and was fulfilled in their lifetime.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, to whom does the Quranic promise in 24:55 refer?
A) All Muslims in general
B) The Companions specifically
C) The prophets
D) The Arabs

Key Takeaway
The Quranic promise of succession and security was fulfilled in the Companions, proving the truth of the Prophet's message.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face fear or uncertainty in your life, do you look for the fulfilled promises of Allah in the Quran as concrete evidence that He is true? Or do you let the fear overshadow your faith? How can you actively recall a specific promise from Allah to strengthen your heart today?
?
This lesson shows that the Companions themselves experienced genuine fear before the promise was fulfilled. Have you ever felt that your faith is weak because you experience fear? How does knowing that the Companions were fearful too change your view of your own struggles, and what step will you take to trust Allah's promise of security?
?
God's promise was not just spiritual but also practical—succession and security in the land. Are you living as if you believe Allah will fulfill His promises in your own life, or do you act only on what you can see? What is one area where you are not trusting His promise, and what will you do this week to rely on His word over your feelings?

Prophethood

Fulfilled Prophecies as Proofs of Prophethood
Sanusi lists multiple fulfilled prophecies as evidence of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's accurate predictions of future events serve as concrete proofs of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophecies fulfilled exactly as foretold confirm divine knowledge.

Sanusi presents several well-known predictions made by the Prophet that came true precisely. These are not mere coincidences but verifiable events that demonstrate the Prophet's access to unseen knowledge, thus proving his prophethood. This lesson examines each example and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its rhythm, then read the literal translation to understand each prophecy mentioned.
Notice that Sanusi uses a concise style.
2
Identify each prophecy and its fulfillment
Go through the passage and list each prediction along with how it came true. There are five distinct examples.
The prophecies include the caliphate duration, following Abu Bakr and Umar, the killing of 'Ammar, al-'Abbas's secret wealth, and an-Najashi's death.
3
Consider how each demonstrates knowledge of the unseen
For each prophecy, ask yourself: could this knowledge have been acquired through normal means? If not, it points to divine revelation.
The specific details (e.g., hidden wealth, simultaneous death news) exceed ordinary human knowledge.
4
Reflect on the cumulative proof
Think about how multiple independent predictions, all fulfilled, strengthen the case for prophethood beyond a single event.
Sanusi notes that such predictions are 'abundant and well-known'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الذي ورد في الأخبار : فمنه : قولُهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ : « الْخِلَافَةُ بَعْدِي ثَلَاثُونَ سَنَةٌ » (۲) ، وكانَتْ خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين هذا القدر (۳) وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « أَقْتَدُوا بِاللَّذَيْنِ بَعْدِي ؛ أَبِي بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ » (٤) ، وهذا إخبارٌ عن بقائهما بعدَهُ ، فكانَ ذلكَ وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لعمَّارٍ رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : « تَقْتُلُكَ الْفِئَةُ الْبَاغِيَةُ » (٥) ، فقُتِلَ معَ علي رضي الله عنهُ يومَ صفّينَ ، وهذا أيضاً يدلُّ على خلافة عليّ رضي الله تعالى عنه بعدَهُ (٦) وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام للعبَّاسِ حِينَ أَسْرَهُ : « أَفْدِ نَفْسَكَ ؛ إِنَّكَ ذُو مَالٍ » ، فقالَ : لا مالَ عندي ، فقال صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أَيْنَ الْمَالُ الَّذِي وَضَعْتَ عِنْدَ أُمِّ الْفَضْل وَلَيْسَ مَعَكُمَا آخَرُ ، فَقُلْتَ : إِنْ أُصِبْتُ فِي سَفَرِي فَلِلْفَضْلِ كَذَا وَلِعَبْدِ اللَّهِ كَذَا ؟! » ، فقال العباس : والذي بعثَكَ بالحقِّ ؛ ما علمَ هذا أحدٌ غيري ، وإِنَّكَ لرسولُ اللهِ ، وأسلم (١) . ومنها : إخباره عن موتِ النجاشي حينَ موتِهِ (۳) ، ونحو هذا ممَّا هو كثير مشهور .
As for what is reported in tradition: among them is his saying, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years.' And the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was this amount. And his saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.' And this is an informing of their remaining after him, and so it was. And his saying, peace be upon him to 'Ammar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'The rebellious party will kill you.' So he was killed with 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, on the day of Siffin. And this also indicates the caliphate of 'Ali after him. And his saying, peace be upon him, to al-'Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself, for you are a man of wealth.' He said: 'I have no wealth.' The Prophet, peace be upon him said: 'Where is the wealth that you placed with Umm al-Fadl, and there was no one else with you? And you said: If I am killed in my travel, then for al-Fadl such-and-such, and for 'Abdullah such-and-such?' So al-'Abbas said: 'By Him who sent you with truth, no one knows this but me, and you are indeed the Messenger of Allah,' and he became Muslim. And among them: his informing of the death of an-Najashi at the time of his death. And the like of this which is abundant and well-known.
Source pages p. 594

Commentary
This passage enumerates multiple instances where the Prophet Muhammad accurately predicted future events, demonstrating knowledge of the unseen (al-ghayb) and thus proving his prophethood. Firstly, he foretold that the caliphate would last thirty years, which matched the rule of the Rightly Guided Caliphs including Hasan. Secondly, he instructed to follow Abu Bakr and Umar after him, which came true as they succeeded him. Thirdly, he told 'Ammar that he would be killed by the rebellious party, which occurred in the Battle of Siffin with 'Ali; this also establishes 'Ali's rightful caliphate. Fourthly, he revealed to al-'Abbas the secret arrangement of his wealth that only al-'Abbas knew, prompting al-'Abbas to embrace Islam. Fifthly, he announced the death of an-Najashi at the very moment it occurred. Sanusi concludes that such predictions are abundant and well-known, serving as clear proofs.

Key Terms
الخلفاء الراشدون
الخبر بالغيب
الفئة الباغية
صفين
النجاشي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These predictions could be coincidences or lucky guesses.
Correction: The specific, verifiable details (e.g., hidden wealth, simultaneous news of death) cannot be known through normal means, so they are deliberate proofs of divine knowledge.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as a fulfilled prophecy in this passage?
A) The caliphate lasting thirty years
B) Abu Bakr and Umar succeeding the Prophet
C) The conquest of Mecca
D) The death of an-Najashi at the time of his death

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate predictions of future events are clear and cumulative proofs of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet knew exactly where al-'Abbas had hidden his wealth—something only al-'Abbas himself knew. Now think: what secrets do you hide in your heart that you believe no one knows? If the Prophet could know such details, what does that say about the One who sent him? Will you let this truth penetrate your denial today?
?
When you read that the caliphate lasted exactly thirty years as foretold, do you realize that Allah's promises never fail? Is there a promise of Allah you have been doubting in your life? What step will you take today to trust it fully?
?
Imagine being 'Ammar, hearing the Prophet say 'the rebellious party will kill you' years before Siffin. Would you have the courage to fight knowing your fate? What does this prophecy teach you about your own life's appointed time? Are you living as if every moment is a gift from the One who knows when your end will come?

Proof from the Prophet's Extraordinary Wisdom
Sanusi presents the proof from the Prophet's extraordinary wisdom, dividing it into theoretical and practical categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unmatched wisdom, acquired without learning, serves as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sudden, unparalleled wisdom is a divine gift, proving his prophethood.

In this passage, Sanusi presents the third proof of prophethood: the Prophet's extraordinary wisdom. He divides wisdom into theoretical and practical, and argues that the Prophet attained a level no rational person could reach in hundreds of years, without any formal education or association with scholars. This miraculous attainment points directly to divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the division of wisdom
Recognize that Sanusi splits wisdom into theoretical (knowledge of God, His attributes, names, rulings) and practical (ethics, bodily politics, management of creation).
This division covers all essential knowledge.
2
Grasp the superlative attainment
Note that the Prophet reached a level unattainable by rational people even after hundreds of years of effort.
3
Recognize the manner of acquisition
The Prophet gained this wisdom suddenly, without learning or mixing with knowledgeable people.
This excludes natural means.
4
Connect to the proof
This extraordinary phenomenon can only be from God, thus proving his prophethood.
The argument is a miracle proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالثُ : أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ قد بلغ في الحكمةِ النظريَّةِ ؛ كمعرفةِ اللهِ تعالى وصفاتِهِ وأسمائه وأحكامه ، وفي الحكمة العملية ؛ وهي علم الأخلاقِ وسياسة البدن وتدبير أمْرِ الخلْقِ.. المبلغ العظيم الذي لا يمكنُ العقلاء الوصول إليه في مئينَ مِنَ السنينَ ، ووصل هو إليه بغتةً مِنْ غيرِ تعلم ولا مخالطة لأحدٍ معروف بالعلم .
The third aspect: that he, peace be upon him, attained in theoretical wisdom – such as knowledge of Allah Almighty and His attributes and names and rulings – and in practical wisdom – which is the science of ethics, the politics of the body, and the management of the affairs of creation – the great attainment which rational people cannot reach in hundreds of years, and he reached it suddenly without learning or mixing with anyone known for knowledge.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the Prophet's extraordinary wisdom (hikma). Sanusi divides wisdom into theoretical (knowledge of God, His attributes, names, and rulings) and practical (ethics, personal conduct, and governance). The Prophet attained such a level that rational people could not reach in hundreds of years, yet he achieved it instantly, without formal learning or association with scholars. This sudden, profound knowledge can only be from divine revelation, establishing his prophethood.

Key Terms
الحكمة النظرية
الحكمة العملية
الأخلاق
سياسة البدن
تدبير الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's wisdom was merely a result of natural intelligence or hard work.
Correction: It was a sudden, supernaturally granted knowledge unattainable by normal means.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, how did the Prophet acquire his wisdom?
A) Through years of study with famous teachers
B) By traveling and learning from multiple cultures
C) Suddenly, without learning or mixing with learned people
D) By receiving inherited knowledge from previous prophets

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sudden, peerless wisdom, acquired without learning, is a divine proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe the Prophet's wisdom was divinely given, yet how often do you seek that same divine guidance in your daily decisions? Write down one practical choice this week where you will consciously turn to Allah's teaching before relying on your own mind.
?
The Prophet attained both theoretical and practical wisdom instantly. Your knowledge of Islam may have taken years, but does it transform your ethics and daily interactions? Identify one area where your behavior does not match what you know, and commit to a specific change today.
?
If the Prophet's wisdom was impossible for hundreds of years of human effort, how arrogant is it to think your own plans and intellect are sufficient? When you face a problem, do you first assume you know the answer, or do you humbly ask Allah to teach you? Challenge yourself to pray for wisdom before every important decision this week.

The Proof from Physical Miracles: The Splitting of the Moon
Sanusi introduces the fourth proof: physical miracles, with one clear example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how physical miracles, such as the splitting of the moon, serve as a proof of prophethood in Sanusi's argument, even though the passage is incomplete.

Core Idea
Physical miracles are tangible signs that confirm the truth of a prophet's claim.

This brief passage introduces the fourth proof in Sanusi's series: the physical miracles (mu'jizat) performed by the Prophet Muhammad. Though the text is cut off, it clearly mentions the splitting of the moon, one of the most famous miracles. This lesson will help you appreciate how such sensory events function as evidence for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Carefully read the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice that the passage is incomplete—it ends abruptly after 'وتسليمِ'.
The missing word is likely 'الحجر' (the stone) or 'الشجر' (the tree), referring to a miracle where objects greeted the Prophet.
2
Identify the proof's structure
Sanusi states that miracles were transmitted (نُقِلَ) from the Prophet. This is the fourth proof. The examples are meant to demonstrate that such events are historically attested.
3
Reflect on the significance of physical miracles
Physical miracles are observable events that break natural laws, serving as direct evidence of divine support for a prophet. They are a key argument in Islamic theology for establishing prophethood.
The splitting of the moon is considered a major miracle in Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الرابع : أنَّهُ نُقِلَ عنه معجزات؛ كانشقاق القمرِ (۳) ، وتسليمِ [؟] .
The fourth aspect: that miracles were transmitted from him; such as the splitting of the moon, and the greeting [of the stone?] [unclear].
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage introduces the fourth proof: physical miracles (mu'jizat) reported from the Prophet. It specifically mentions the splitting of the moon, a well-known miracle. It also begins to mention another miracle ('the greeting' presumably of the stone or tree) but the text is incomplete. This proof requires further reference to complete the argument.

Key Terms
المعجزات
انشقاق القمر
تسليم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are not needed as proofs because prophethood is established by reason alone.
Correction: While reason can establish the possibility of prophethood, actual miracles provide sensory confirmation that a particular person is indeed a prophet, as Sanusi argues here.

Checkpoint
Which miracle is explicitly mentioned in this incomplete passage?
A) The water gushing from the Prophet's fingers
B) The splitting of the moon
C) The speaking of the wolf
D) The crying of the palm trunk

Key Takeaway
Physical miracles like the splitting of the moon are transmitted proofs that validate a prophet's mission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the splitting of the moon is a transmitted miracle, do you accept it as a historical fact that truly happened? If you hesitate, what is the foundation of your belief in the prophethood of Muhammad?
?
The companions had physical signs to strengthen their faith. What tangible evidence are you relying on today for your certainty in the Prophet—or are you coasting on habit?

The Prophet's Unlearned Wisdom as Proof of Prophethood
Sanusi presents the third proof of prophethood: the Prophet's unprecedented wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet Muhammad's (peace be upon him) extraordinary wisdom, attained without human instruction, serves as a rational proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's wisdom came directly from Allah, not from human teachers.

Sanusi now presents the third rational proof for prophethood: the Prophet's unparalleled wisdom in both theoretical and practical matters. This wisdom was so profound that no human could achieve it in a lifetime, yet the Prophet possessed it suddenly without any teacher. This passage invites us to see divine action in the Prophet's knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the two types of wisdom
The passage distinguishes between theoretical wisdom (knowledge of God, His attributes, names, rulings) and practical wisdom (ethics, bodily governance, management of creation). Notice each definition.
3
Understand the scale of attainment
Sanusi says the Prophet reached a level that rational people cannot reach in hundreds of years. Reflect on what this implies about the Prophet's knowledge.
4
Notice how the knowledge was acquired
The key phrase is 'suddenly without learning nor mixing with anyone known for knowledge.' This absence of a human teacher is central to the argument.
5
Consider why this is a proof
Ask yourself: If the Prophet's wisdom exceeds normal human capacity and was acquired without human means, what must be its source? The commentary will help you see the conclusion.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالثُ : أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ قد بلغ في الحكمة النظريَّةِ ؛ كمعرفةِ اللهِ تعالى وصفاتِهِ وأسمائه وأحكامه ، وفي الحكمة العملية ؛ وهي علم الأخلاقِ وسياسة البدن وتدبير أمْرِ الخلْقِ.. المبلغ العظيم الذي لا يمكنُ العقلاء الوصول إليه في مئينَ مِنَ السنينَ ، ووصل هو إليه بغتةً مِنْ غيرِ تعلم ولا مخالطة لأحدٍ معروف بالعلم .
The third aspect: that he, peace and blessings be upon him, attained in theoretical wisdom – such as knowledge of God Most High, His attributes, His names, and His rulings – and in practical wisdom – which is the science of ethics, governance of the body, and management of the creation – the immense level that rational people cannot reach in hundreds of years, and he reached it suddenly without learning nor mixing with anyone known for knowledge.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof of the Prophet's prophethood. It is a rational argument based on the extraordinary wisdom that the Prophet (peace be upon him) possessed. Sanusi divides wisdom into two types: theoretical (النظريّة) and practical (العملية). Theoretical wisdom includes knowledge of God, His attributes, names, and legal rulings. Practical wisdom includes ethics, bodily governance, and managing the affairs of people. The Prophet attained both types to a degree that is impossible for ordinary intelligent people to reach even in hundreds of years. Moreover, he acquired this wisdom suddenly (بغتة) without any prior learning or association with a known scholar. This points to divine origin, as human learning cannot produce such immediate and profound wisdom without a teacher. Sanusi does not provide a separate conclusion, but the argument is complete in itself: the Prophet's wisdom is a miracle (mu'jizah) because it exceeds normal human capacity and occurs through divine assistance.

Key Terms
الحكمة النظريّة
الحكمة العملية
بغتة
معروف بالعلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Prophet acquired his knowledge through human teachers or long study.
Correction: The passage explicitly states he reached wisdom 'without learning nor mixing with anyone known for knowledge,' showing his knowledge was directly from Allah.

Checkpoint
What does the Prophet's attainment of theoretical and practical wisdom without learning demonstrate?
A) That he was naturally intelligent.
B) That his knowledge was of divine origin, proving his prophethood.
C) That he studied secretly.
D) That wisdom is irrelevant to prophethood.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's sudden acquisition of unmatched wisdom without a human teacher is a miracle that proves his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the Prophet’s wisdom came directly from Allah without any human teacher. Do you seek wisdom from Allah through the Quran and Sunnah with the same humility, or do you rely on your own intellect and the praise of people? Will you commit to spending time today asking Allah for beneficial knowledge?
?
The Prophet attained immense wisdom suddenly. When was the last time you felt a sudden, deep understanding of your faith that you could not attribute to your own effort? Did you thank Allah for that gift? If not, stop now and ask Him to grant you such wisdom, and promise to use it for His sake.
?
If the Prophet’s knowledge was unlearned and from Allah, then what does that say about the knowledge you have acquired? Are you proud of your degrees or teachers, or do you recognize that all true knowledge is from Allah? Make a silent intention to attribute every bit of your understanding to Him alone.

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
The Prophet's Many Miracles as Proof
Sanusi enumerates miracles as proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's numerous miracles, widely transmitted, serve as a compelling proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The multiplicity and widespread transmission of miracles make denial unreasonable.

Sanusi presents the fourth proof of prophethood: the many miracles attributed to the Prophet. These miracles range from cosmic events to everyday objects, and their wide attestation in hadith literature, often through multiple chains, elevates them to certainty. This lesson examines this argument and the key miracles listed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the list of miracles and the concluding statement about their widespread transmission.
The passage is from a kalam text, so it is concise and argumentative.
2
Identify the miracles mentioned
Sanusi lists several miracles. Identify each one: splitting of the moon, glorification of pebbles, revival of the dead, multiplication of food, water from fingers, moaning palm trunk, complaint of she-camel, testimony of poisoned sheep.
These are well-known miracles from hadith.
3
Understand the role of tawatur
Sanusi ends by noting that these miracles are well-known and some have reached tawatur (mass transmission). This means they are so widely reported that their truth is certain.
Tawatur is a key concept in Islamic epistemology for establishing certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الرابع : أنَّهُ نُقِلَ عنه معجزات ؛ كانشقاق القمر (۳) ، وتسليمِ [؟] الخارجون عن الإمام [؟] ، فعُلِمَ أن عليّاً كرم الله وجهه هو الإمام الحق [؟] حامدي » ( ٤٨٣ ) (۱) رواه أبو نعيم في " دلائل النبوة " ( ٤١٠ ) . (۲) رواه البخاري ( ۱۳۱۸ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه (۳) رواه البخاري ( ٣٦٣٦ ) ، ومسلم ( ۲۸۰۰ ) من حديث سيدنا ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه . الحجر (1) [؟] الموتى (٤) (۲) وانقياد الشجر وتسبيح الحصــا(٣) ، وإحياء وتكثير الطعام القليل (٥) ، ونبوع الماءِ مِنْ بين (v) [؟] أصابعه (٦) (۷) وحنين الجذع ، وشكاية الناقة(۸) ، وشهادة الشاة المسمومة (۹) ، إلى غير ذلكَ ممَّا لا ينحصر ، وهو مشهور مستفيض في كتب الأحاديثِ ، وبعضُه وصل التواتر . (۱) رواه مسلم ( ۲۲۷۷ ) من حديث سيدنا جابر بن سمرة رضي الله عنه . (٤) كخبر إحياء والديه الكريمين عليه الصلاة والسلام ، ومن ذلك ما رواه ابن شاهين في ( الناسخ والمنسوخ ) ( ٦٥٦ ) في إحياء السيدة آمنة رضي الله عنها من حديث الصديقة عائشة رضي الله عنها ، وهو خبر ضعيف لا موضوع ذلك مال جماعة من أعلام الحفاظ ؛ كالخطيب البغدادي ، وابن عساكر ، وابن شاهين ، وأبي القاسم السهيلي ، والقرطبي ، ومحب الدين الطبري ، وناصر الدين بن المنير ، وفتح الدين بن سيد الناس ، وشمس الدين بن ناصر الدين الدمشقي ، وانظر ( سبل الهدى والرشاد ) ( ١ / ٢٦٠ ) (5) أخباره صلى الله عليه وسلم في ذلك كثيرة شهيرة ؛ منها : إطعامه أهل الخندق كلهم وإشباعهم من شاة لسيدنا جابر معَ صاع شعير ، روى ذلك البخاري ( ٤٠١٢ ) ومسلم ( ٢٠٣٩ ) (٦) رواه البخاري (۲۰۰) ، ومسلم (۲۲۷۹) من حديث سيدنا أنس رضي الله عنه (۷) رواه البخاري ( ٣٥٨٣ ) من حديث سيدنا ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما (۸) رواه أبو داود ( ٢٥٤٩ ) من حديث سيدنا عبد الله بن جعفر رضي الله عنهما (۹) رواه البخاري ( ٢٦١٧ ) ، ومسلم ( ۲۱۹۰ ) من حديث سيدنا أنس رضي الله عنه
The fourth aspect: that miracles were transmitted from him, such as the splitting of the moon (3), and the surrender of [؟] those outside the imam [؟], so it was known that Ali, may God honor his face, is the true Imam [؟] Hamidi (483). (1) Narrated by Abu Nuʿaym in 'Dalaʾil al-Nubuwwa' (410). (2) Narrated by al-Bukhari (1318) from the hadith of our master Abu Hurayra, may God be pleased with him. (3) Narrated by al-Bukhari (3636) and Muslim (2800) from the hadith of our master Ibn Masʿud, may God be pleased with him. The stone (1) [؟] the dead (4) (2) and the compliance of trees and the glorification of pebbles (3), and the revival and multiplication of little food (5), and the gushing forth of water from between (v) [؟] his fingers (6) (7) and the moaning of the palm trunk, and the complaint of the she-camel (8), and the testimony of the poisoned sheep (9), and beyond that which is not limited, and it is well-known and widespread in the books of hadith, and some of it has reached tawatur (mass transmission). (1) Narrated by Muslim (2277) from the hadith of our master Jabir ibn Samura, may God be pleased with him. (2) Narrated by Muslim (3012) from the hadith of our master Jabir, may God be pleased with him. (3) Narrated by al-Tabarani in 'al-Muʿjam al-Awsat' (1244, 4097) from the hadith of our master Abu Dharr al-Ghifari, may God be pleased with him. (4) Such as the report of reviving his two noble parents, peace and blessings be upon him, and among that is what Ibn Shahin narrated in 'al-Nasikh wa al-Mansukh' (656) concerning the revival of Lady Amina, may God be pleased with her, from the hadith of al-Siddiqa ʿAʾisha, may God be pleased with her, and it is a weak report, not a fabricated one, according to a group of leading authorities; such as al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, Ibn ʿAsakir, Ibn Shahin, Abu al-Qasim al-Suhayli, al-Qurtubi, Muhibb al-Din al-Tabari, Nasir al-Din ibn al-Munir, Fath al-Din ibn Sayyid al-Nas, Shams al-Din ibn Nasir al-Din al-Dimashqi; and see 'Subul al-Huda wa al-Rashad' (1/260). (5) His reports, peace be upon him, in that regard are many and famous; among them: his feeding all the people of al-Khandaq and satiating them from a sheep belonging to our master Jabir with a saʿ of barley; that was narrated by al-Bukhari (4012) and Muslim (2039). (6) Narrated by al-Bukhari (200) and Muslim (2279) from the hadith of our master Anas, may God be pleased with him. (7) Narrated by al-Bukhari (3583) from the hadith of our master Ibn ʿUmar, may God be pleased with them both. (8) Narrated by Abu Dawud (2549) from the hadith of our master ʿAbd Allah ibn Jaʿfar, may God be pleased with them both. (9) Narrated by al-Bukhari (2617) and Muslim (2190) from the hadith of our master Anas, may God be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof of prophethood: the multitude of miracles transmitted from the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). Sanusi begins by stating that miracles were transmitted from him (نُقِلَ عنه معجزات). He then lists several examples: the splitting of the moon (a famous miracle), and then a confusing phrase about 'surrender of those outside the imam' which may be an interpolation or marginal note. The text then jumps to a list of miracles on page 596: the glorification of pebbles (تسبيح الحصا), revival of the dead (إحياء الموتى), multiplication of little food, water gushing from between his fingers, the moaning of the palm trunk, the complaint of the she-camel, and the testimony of the poisoned sheep. Sanusi notes that these miracles are numerous beyond enumeration, well-known and widespread in hadith books, and some have reached tawatur (mass transmission, i.e., certainty). The footnotes included provide references for each miracle and discuss the authenticity of certain reports, such as the revival of the Prophet's parents, which is considered weak but not fabricated. However, these footnotes are later additions; the main argument is simply that the multiplicity and widespread transmission of these miracles prove the Prophet's truthfulness. The lesson follows a typical kalam method: providing empirical evidence (transmitted reports) to support a rational claim. The sheer number and variety of miracles, many attested by multiple chains, make denial unreasonable.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what strengthens the authenticity of the Prophet's miracles?
A) They are all in the Quran.
B) They are few in number.
C) They are widely transmitted, with some reaching tawatur.
D) They were witnessed only by family.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's multiple miracles, many mass-transmitted, constitute a definitive proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have heard about the splitting of the moon many times, but do you live as if it actually happened? If you were absolutely certain that it did, would that change anything about how you obey the Prophet today? What is one specific commandment you have been neglecting that you will now fulfill, because this miracle proves his truthfulness?
?
The lesson emphasizes that many of these miracles have reached tawatur—they are as certain as the sun rising. Has that certainty ever entered your heart, or do you still treat them as mere stories? What would it look like for you to truly internalize that these events are undeniable history, not just faith claims?
?
You believe in the Prophet's miracles, but does that belief actually shape your decisions? When you are about to sin, do you think: 'The Prophet who split the moon commanded me to avoid this'? If not, what is blocking that connection, and what step will you take today to make his miracles a living reality in your daily choices?

First Evidence: Lifelong Truthfulness
First evidence from Prophet's truthfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unwavering truthfulness serves as a rational proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Truthfulness so consistent that even enemies testified to it.

Sanusi begins the fifth argument for prophethood by pointing to the Prophet's biography and attributes. The first and most foundational attribute is his lifelong truthfulness, which was so absolute that no one ever heard a lie from him, and his enemies themselves admitted it. This lesson examines that evidence and its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly, noting the emphasis on 'ملازمة الصدق' and the two supporting reasons.
The passage uses a logical structure: assertion then proof.
2
Understand the two arguments
The first reason: no one ever heard a lie. The second: even enemies would have exposed any falsehood. Recognize how these cumulative observations make a strong case.
Enemy testimony is especially powerful in historical proof.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: if the Prophet had ever lied, wouldn't his enemies have used that against him? Their silence confirms his truthfulness.
This is an argument from absence of evidence against.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الخامس : الاستدلال بسيرته وأوصافه التي تواترت إلينا ، وهي كثيرة : أحدها : ملازمة الصدق من أول عمره إلى آخره ، فإن أحداً ما سمع منه كذبة قط ، وقد اعترف له أعداؤه بذلك ، وأيضاً لو صدر منه الكذب ولو مرة في عمره لنبزه أعداؤه بذلك . وثانيها : ترك الدنيا والإعراض عنها وعن زخارفها على الدوام ، حتى إن قريشاً عرضوا عليه المال والزوجة والرئاسة لترك هذه الدعوى . . فلم يلتفت إليها . وثالثها : كان في أعظم الدرجات في السخاوة ، حتى إنه سبحانه عاتبه عليها بقوله : وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ [الإسراء : ٢٩] ، والشجاعة ، حتى إنه لم يفر قط ولا تزحزح للفرار في معركة قط حتى في يوم أحد ونحوه مما عظم فيه الرعب . ورابعها : كان في غاية الفصاحة والبلاغة ؛ حتى إن فصاحته قد أعيت بلغاء الخطباء من العرب العرباء ، ولذا قال : « أُوتِيتُ جَوَامِعَ الْكَلِمِ ». وخامسها : أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام تحمل في أداء الرسالة أنواعاً من المشاق والمتاعب لا يثبت معها إلا من هو على الحق من الله تعالى ، وهو مع ذلك مصر على دعوى الرسالة ، ولم يظهر في عزمه فتور ، ولا في إصراره قصور . وسادسها : أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان مع أهل الدنيا في غاية الترفع ، ومع الفقراء والمساكين في غاية التواضع . وسابعها : ما كان عليه من حسن الخلق ، حتى إنه لا يزداد مع الغضب إلا حلماً . وثامنها : حسن ذاته الكريمة ، وما اشتملت عليه من المحاسن التي هي خرق عادة ، ولم توجد لبشر سواه . وما أحسن قول عبد الله بن رواحة الأنصاري رضي الله عنه في ذلك يشير إلى محاسنه صلى الله عليه وسلم خلقاً وخلقا : [ من البسيط] لو لم تَكُنْ فِيهِ آيَاتٌ مُبَيَّنَةٌ لَكَانَ مَنْظَرُهُ يُنْبِيكَ بِالْخَبَرِ . ولقد أسلم أبو ذر رضي الله عنه عند رؤيته إياه ، وقال : ( لا
The fifth aspect: inference from his biography and attributes which have been reported to us successively (mutawatir), and they are many: First: his persistent truthfulness from the beginning of his life to its end, for no one ever heard a lie from him, and his enemies testified to that. Also, if a lie had occurred from him even once in his life, his enemies would have reproached him for it. Second: his renunciation of this world and turning away from it and its adornments continually, such that the Quraysh offered him wealth, marriage, and leadership to abandon this claim, but he paid no attention to them. Third: he was at the highest degree of generosity, so much so that Allah Almighty reproached him for it by His saying: "And do not stretch it forth completely" [al-Isra 17:29]; and [he was at the highest degree] of courage, so much so that he never fled nor budged to flee in any battle, not even on the day of Uhud and similar days when terror was great. Fourth: he was at the utmost eloquence and rhetoric, such that his eloquence defeated the eloquent orators of the pure Arabs, and therefore he said: "I have been given concise speech." Fifth: he, peace and blessings be upon him, bore in delivering the message various kinds of hardships and difficulties that none can endure except one who is upon the truth from Allah Almighty, and despite that he persisted in his claim to prophethood, and no weakness appeared in his resolve nor any deficiency in his perseverance. Sixth: he, peace and blessings be upon him, was with the people of the world at the utmost dignity, and with the poor and needy at the utmost humility. Seventh: his good character, such that when angered, he only increased in forbearance. Eighth: the beauty of his noble person and what it contained of perfections that are a breach of custom and not found in any other human being. How excellent is the saying of Abdullah ibn Rawaha al-Ansari, may Allah be pleased with him, indicating his perfections, peace be upon him, in form and character: [al-Basit] "If there were no clear signs in him, his appearance alone would inform you of the truth." And Abu Dharr, may Allah be pleased with him, embraced Islam upon seeing him, and said: (no
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof of prophethood, which is inference from the Prophet's biography and attributes that have reached us via successive transmission (tawatur). The author lists eight specific evidences drawn from the Prophet's life. The first is his lifelong truthfulness, which was acknowledged even by enemies and which would have been used against him if ever violated. The second is his complete renunciation of worldly pleasures despite being offered great inducements. The third combines two attributes: generosity (to the point of divine gentle reproof in Qur'an 17:29) and courage (never fleeing in battle). The fourth is his unmatched eloquence, confirmed by his own statement about being given 'concise speech.' The fifth is his endurance of hardships in delivering the message—a sign of divine support. The sixth is his perfect balance of dignity toward the worldly and humility toward the poor. The seventh is his forbearance under anger. The eighth is the supernatural beauty and perfection of his person, which was unprecedented. The passage concludes with a poetic testimony from a Companion and the historical example of Abu Dharr embracing Islam solely upon seeing the Prophet's appearance, which itself indicated his truthfulness.

Key Terms
ملازمة الصدق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that truthfulness alone does not prove prophethood, as many truthful people exist.
Correction: The argument is not just that he was truthful, but that his truthfulness was so complete and universally acknowledged that it becomes evidence of divine support.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would have happened if the Prophet had lied even once?
A) His followers would have left him
B) His enemies would have reproached him
C) He would have repented
D) The revelation would have stopped

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's unparalleled truthfulness, acknowledged by friends and foes alike, is a strong rational proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any area of your life where you are not consistently truthful? How can you emulate the Prophet's lifelong truthfulness starting today?
?
If your enemies were to testify about your character, what would they say? Would they acknowledge your truthfulness?
?
The passage argues that if the Prophet had ever lied, his enemies would have exploited it. Do you realize that your own lies, even if undiscovered, eventually damage your credibility and witness for Islam? What lie do you need to confess and abandon today?

Second Evidence: Renunciation of the World
Second evidence: renunciation of worldly pleasures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's complete disinterest in worldly offers strengthens the proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
He turned down wealth, marriage, and leadership for the sake of truth.

The second evidence focuses on the Prophet's detachment from worldly pleasures. Despite enticing offers from the Quraysh, he remained steadfast. This lesson examines how such renunciation indicates sincerity and divine support.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the description of his renunciation and the specific offers made by Quraysh.
Note the contrast: worldly power vs. divine mission.
2
Understand the significance of the offers
The Quraysh offered wealth, marriage, and leadership. These were things he could have accepted without losing his claim, yet he refused.
This shows he was not motivated by personal gain.
3
Reflect on the implication
Why would someone reject such attractive offers unless they were absolutely convinced of their mission from God?
This is a sign of truthfulness and divine backing.

Misconception & Correction

A) Wealth, marriage, and leadership
B) A kingdom and army
C) Safety and protection
D) Religious authority

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's rejection of substantial worldly inducements indicates that his mission was not for personal benefit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were offered something you deeply desire—wealth, a marriage, or a leadership role—on the condition that you abandon a truth you hold, would you reject it as the Prophet did? What would that cost you, and what would it gain you?
?
The Prophet paid no attention to the offers. What worldly distractions or temptations currently occupy your attention that might be pulling you away from your deen? How can you begin to 'pay no attention' to them starting today?
?
Reflect on a moment when you compromised a truth for a worldly benefit. How did that feel afterwards? Now imagine the opposite: if you had rejected it like the Prophet, how might your life and heart be different? Will you commit to one small act of renunciation this week?

Third Evidence: Generosity and Courage
Third evidence: generosity and courage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's extraordinary generosity and courage serve as evidence of his prophethood.

Core Idea
His generosity drew divine reproach; his courage never faltered.

The third evidence combines two attributes: generosity so extreme that Allah gently reproached him, and courage so unwavering that he never fled from battle even in the most terrifying moments. This lesson examines how these qualities point to divine support.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the description of his generosity and courage, noting the Qur'anic reference and the battle of Uhud.
The reproach from Allah indicates the extraordinary level of generosity.
2
Understand the generosity evidence
Allah said 'Do not stretch it forth completely' (17:29), which is a gentle rebuke for over-generosity. This implies his generosity was superhuman.
The verse is not condemning generosity but setting a balance.
3
Reflect on the courage evidence
He never fled from battle, even at Uhud when the Muslims were terrified. This courage is not natural; it suggests divine aid.
Courage in such extreme circumstances is a sign of truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الخامس : الاستدلال بسيرته وأوصافه التي تواترت إلينا ، وهي كثيرة : أحدها : ملازمة الصدق من أول عمره إلى آخره ، فإن أحداً ما سمع منه كذبة قط ، وقد اعترف له أعداؤه بذلك ، وأيضاً لو صدر منه الكذب ولو مرة في عمره لنبزه أعداؤه بذلك . وثانيها : ترك الدنيا والإعراض عنها وعن زخارفها على الدوام ، حتى إن قريشاً عرضوا عليه المال والزوجة والرئاسة لترك هذه الدعوى . . فلم يلتفت إليها . وثالثها : كان في أعظم الدرجات في السخاوة ، حتى إنه سبحانه عاتبه عليها بقوله : وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ [الإسراء : ٢٩] ، والشجاعة ، حتى إنه لم يفر قط ولا تزحزح للفرار في معركة قط حتى في يوم أحد ونحوه مما عظم فيه الرعب . ورابعها : كان في غاية الفصاحة والبلاغة ؛ حتى إن فصاحته قد أعيت بلغاء الخطباء من العرب العرباء ، ولذا قال : « أُوتِيتُ جَوَامِعَ الْكَلِمِ ». وخامسها : أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام تحمل في أداء الرسالة أنواعاً من المشاق والمتاعب لا يثبت معها إلا من هو على الحق من الله تعالى ، وهو مع ذلك مصر على دعوى الرسالة ، ولم يظهر في عزمه فتور ، ولا في إصراره قصور . وسادسها : أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان مع أهل الدنيا في غاية الترفع ، ومع الفقراء والمساكين في غاية التواضع . وسابعها : ما كان عليه من حسن الخلق ، حتى إنه لا يزداد مع الغضب إلا حلماً . وثامنها : حسن ذاته الكريمة ، وما اشتملت عليه من المحاسن التي هي خرق عادة ، ولم توجد لبشر سواه . وما أحسن قول عبد الله بن رواحة الأنصاري رضي الله عنه في ذلك يشير إلى محاسنه صلى الله عليه وسلم خلقاً وخلقا : [ من البسيط] لو لم تَكُنْ فِيهِ آيَاتٌ مُبَيَّنَةٌ لَكَانَ مَنْظَرُهُ يُنْبِيكَ بِالْخَبَرِ . ولقد أسلم أبو ذر رضي الله عنه عند رؤيته إياه ، وقال : ( لا
The fifth aspect: inference from his biography and attributes which have been reported to us successively (mutawatir), and they are many: First: his persistent truthfulness from the beginning of his life to its end, for no one ever heard a lie from him, and his enemies testified to that. Also, if a lie had occurred from him even once in his life, his enemies would have reproached him for it. Second: his renunciation of this world and turning away from it and its adornments continually, such that the Quraysh offered him wealth, marriage, and leadership to abandon this claim, but he paid no attention to them. Third: he was at the highest degree of generosity, so much so that Allah Almighty reproached him for it by His saying: "And do not stretch it forth completely" [al-Isra 17:29]; and [he was at the highest degree] of courage, so much so that he never fled nor budged to flee in any battle, not even on the day of Uhud and similar days when terror was great. Fourth: he was at the utmost eloquence and rhetoric, such that his eloquence defeated the eloquent orators of the pure Arabs, and therefore he said: "I have been given concise speech." Fifth: he, peace and blessings be upon him, bore in delivering the message various kinds of hardships and difficulties that none can endure except one who is upon the truth from Allah Almighty, and despite that he persisted in his claim to prophethood, and no weakness appeared in his resolve nor any deficiency in his perseverance. Sixth: he, peace and blessings be upon him, was with the people of the world at the utmost dignity, and with the poor and needy at the utmost humility. Seventh: his good character, such that when angered, he only increased in forbearance. Eighth: the beauty of his noble person and what it contained of perfections that are a breach of custom and not found in any other human being. How excellent is the saying of Abdullah ibn Rawaha al-Ansari, may Allah be pleased with him, indicating his perfections, peace be upon him, in form and character: [al-Basit] "If there were no clear signs in him, his appearance alone would inform you of the truth." And Abu Dharr, may Allah be pleased with him, embraced Islam upon seeing him, and said: (no
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof of prophethood, which is inference from the Prophet's biography and attributes that have reached us via successive transmission (tawatur). The author lists eight specific evidences drawn from the Prophet's life. The first is his lifelong truthfulness, which was acknowledged even by enemies and which would have been used against him if ever violated. The second is his complete renunciation of worldly pleasures despite being offered great inducements. The third combines two attributes: generosity (to the point of divine gentle reproof in Qur'an 17:29) and courage (never fleeing in battle). The fourth is his unmatched eloquence, confirmed by his own statement about being given 'concise speech.' The fifth is his endurance of hardships in delivering the message—a sign of divine support. The sixth is his perfect balance of dignity toward the worldly and humility toward the poor. The seventh is his forbearance under anger. The eighth is the supernatural beauty and perfection of his person, which was unprecedented. The passage concludes with a poetic testimony from a Companion and the historical example of Abu Dharr embracing Islam solely upon seeing the Prophet's appearance, which itself indicated his truthfulness.

Key Terms
السخاوة
الشجاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that courage is common; but the Prophet's courage was absolute and never wavered, which is extraordinary.
Correction: His courage in the face of death, especially at Uhud, was superhuman and points to divine assistance.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which battle is mentioned as an example of the Prophet's courage?
A) Badr
B) Uhud
C) Khandaq
D) Khaybar

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's superhuman generosity and courage are signs that he was supported by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet gave so generously that Allah reproached him. Have you ever given until it hurt, or do you hold back for fear of losing? What would it take for you to give like the Prophet?
?
The Prophet never fled from battle, even when terror was great. What is the one fear in your life that makes you want to run away? How can you face it with faith-fueled courage starting this week?
?
Allah reproached the Prophet for his generosity. Are you more afraid of being reproached by people for being too generous or by Allah for being too stingy? Which fear controls your giving?

Fourth Evidence: Eloquence
Fourth evidence: eloquence and rhetoric

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unmatched eloquence serves as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
His eloquence defeated the best Arab orators and was divinely granted.

The fourth evidence is the Prophet's extraordinary eloquence. He was not educated in rhetoric, yet his speech surpassed the most skilled Arab poets and orators. This lesson examines how his gift of 'concise speech' indicates divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the description of his eloquence and the mention of 'Jawami' al-Kalim'.
Note that the Arabs were masters of eloquence, yet they were defeated.
2
Understand the context
The Arabs prided themselves on eloquence. The Prophet's speech was so superior that even the best were unable to match it.
This is a form of miracle (i'jaz).
3
Reflect on the implication
If he were a false prophet, how could he produce such unmatched eloquence without training?
This points to divine inspiration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet's eloquence was a divine gift that defeated the best orators, how seriously do you take his words? Is there a hadith you've heard that you ignore because it demands change? What would it look like for you to submit to every word he spoke?
?
The Arabs recognized his speech as beyond human ability. When you read the Quran or hadith, do you feel that divine weight, or do you treat it as ordinary advice? How would your daily actions change if you truly believed every word came from Allah?
?
The Prophet said 'I have been given concise speech.' If his speech was perfect and concise, how does your own speech compare? Are you wasting words in gossip, arguments, or meaningless talk? Will you commit today to speak only what is beneficial, seeking to reflect divine guidance in your words?

Fifth Evidence: Endurance of Hardships
Fifth evidence: endurance in delivering the message

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's endurance of severe hardships in delivering the message confirms his prophethood.

Core Idea
He bore unbearable hardships without weakening in resolve.

The fifth evidence highlights the Prophet's incredible perseverance in the face of immense trials. Despite persecution, boycott, and loss, he continued his mission without faltering. This lesson examines how such steadfastness indicates divine support and truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the description of the hardships he endured and his unwavering resolve.
Note the phrase 'لا يثبت معها إلا من هو على الحق'.
2
Understand the nature of hardships
He faced exile, hunger, physical harm, and the loss of loved ones. These would break any ordinary person.
The message lists 'أنواعاً من المشاق والمتاعب'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Only someone truly convinced of being on the truth could endure such trials without weakening.
This is a sign of divine support.

Sixth Evidence: Perfect Balance of Dignity and Humility
Sixth evidence: dignity and humility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unique combination of dignity with the wealthy and humility with the poor serves as evidence of his prophethood.

Core Idea
He was majestic with the proud and humble with the poor.

The sixth evidence highlights the Prophet's perfect social balance. He displayed utmost dignity with the worldly powerful, yet was extremely humble with the poor and needy. This rare combination is unnatural in human character and indicates divine guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the description of his behavior with two groups: the worldly and the poor.
Note the contrast between 'غاية الترفع' and 'غاية التواضع'.
2
Understand the balance
Most people are either arrogant with the poor or obsequious with the rich. The Prophet had the perfect balance.
This is a sign of perfect character.
3
Reflect on the implication
Such balanced character is not typical; it suggests a divinely molded personality.
This adds to the cumulative evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الخامس : الاستدلال بسيرته وأوصافه التي تواترت إلينا ، وهي كثيرة : أحدها : ملازمة الصدق من أول عمره إلى آخره ، فإن أحداً ما سمع منه كذبة قط ، وقد اعترف له أعداؤه بذلك ، وأيضاً لو صدر منه الكذب ولو مرة في عمره لنبزه أعداؤه بذلك . وثانيها : ترك الدنيا والإعراض عنها وعن زخارفها على الدوام ، حتى إن قريشاً عرضوا عليه المال والزوجة والرئاسة لترك هذه الدعوى . . فلم يلتفت إليها . وثالثها : كان في أعظم الدرجات في السخاوة ، حتى إنه سبحانه عاتبه عليها بقوله : وَلَا تَبْسُطْهَا كُلَّ الْبَسْطِ [الإسراء : ٢٩] ، والشجاعة ، حتى إنه لم يفر قط ولا تزحزح للفرار في معركة قط حتى في يوم أحد ونحوه مما عظم فيه الرعب . ورابعها : كان في غاية الفصاحة والبلاغة ؛ حتى إن فصاحته قد أعيت بلغاء الخطباء من العرب العرباء ، ولذا قال : « أُوتِيتُ جَوَامِعَ الْكَلِمِ ». وخامسها : أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام تحمل في أداء الرسالة أنواعاً من المشاق والمتاعب لا يثبت معها إلا من هو على الحق من الله تعالى ، وهو مع ذلك مصر على دعوى الرسالة ، ولم يظهر في عزمه فتور ، ولا في إصراره قصور . وسادسها : أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان مع أهل الدنيا في غاية الترفع ، ومع الفقراء والمساكين في غاية التواضع . وسابعها : ما كان عليه من حسن الخلق ، حتى إنه لا يزداد مع الغضب إلا حلماً . وثامنها : حسن ذاته الكريمة ، وما اشتملت عليه من المحاسن التي هي خرق عادة ، ولم توجد لبشر سواه . وما أحسن قول عبد الله بن رواحة الأنصاري رضي الله عنه في ذلك يشير إلى محاسنه صلى الله عليه وسلم خلقاً وخلقا : [ من البسيط] لو لم تَكُنْ فِيهِ آيَاتٌ مُبَيَّنَةٌ لَكَانَ مَنْظَرُهُ يُنْبِيكَ بِالْخَبَرِ . ولقد أسلم أبو ذر رضي الله عنه عند رؤيته إياه ، وقال : ( لا
The fifth aspect: inference from his biography and attributes which have been reported to us successively (mutawatir), and they are many: First: his persistent truthfulness from the beginning of his life to its end, for no one ever heard a lie from him, and his enemies testified to that. Also, if a lie had occurred from him even once in his life, his enemies would have reproached him for it. Second: his renunciation of this world and turning away from it and its adornments continually, such that the Quraysh offered him wealth, marriage, and leadership to abandon this claim, but he paid no attention to them. Third: he was at the highest degree of generosity, so much so that Allah Almighty reproached him for it by His saying: "And do not stretch it forth completely" [al-Isra 17:29]; and [he was at the highest degree] of courage, so much so that he never fled nor budged to flee in any battle, not even on the day of Uhud and similar days when terror was great. Fourth: he was at the utmost eloquence and rhetoric, such that his eloquence defeated the eloquent orators of the pure Arabs, and therefore he said: "I have been given concise speech." Fifth: he, peace and blessings be upon him, bore in delivering the message various kinds of hardships and difficulties that none can endure except one who is upon the truth from Allah Almighty, and despite that he persisted in his claim to prophethood, and no weakness appeared in his resolve nor any deficiency in his perseverance. Sixth: he, peace and blessings be upon him, was with the people of the world at the utmost dignity, and with the poor and needy at the utmost humility. Seventh: his good character, such that when angered, he only increased in forbearance. Eighth: the beauty of his noble person and what it contained of perfections that are a breach of custom and not found in any other human being. How excellent is the saying of Abdullah ibn Rawaha al-Ansari, may Allah be pleased with him, indicating his perfections, peace be upon him, in form and character: [al-Basit] "If there were no clear signs in him, his appearance alone would inform you of the truth." And Abu Dharr, may Allah be pleased with him, embraced Islam upon seeing him, and said: (no
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof of prophethood, which is inference from the Prophet's biography and attributes that have reached us via successive transmission (tawatur). The author lists eight specific evidences drawn from the Prophet's life. The first is his lifelong truthfulness, which was acknowledged even by enemies and which would have been used against him if ever violated. The second is his complete renunciation of worldly pleasures despite being offered great inducements. The third combines two attributes: generosity (to the point of divine gentle reproof in Qur'an 17:29) and courage (never fleeing in battle). The fourth is his unmatched eloquence, confirmed by his own statement about being given 'concise speech.' The fifth is his endurance of hardships in delivering the message—a sign of divine support. The sixth is his perfect balance of dignity toward the worldly and humility toward the poor. The seventh is his forbearance under anger. The eighth is the supernatural beauty and perfection of his person, which was unprecedented. The passage concludes with a poetic testimony from a Companion and the historical example of Abu Dharr embracing Islam solely upon seeing the Prophet's appearance, which itself indicated his truthfulness.

Key Terms
التواضع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that such balance is just good manners, but it is extremely rare and consistent.
Correction: The perfect balance between dignity and humility, without any excess, is a sign of divine guidance.

Checkpoint
How did the Prophet behave with the poor according to the passage?
A) With utmost dignity
B) With utmost humility
C) With indifference
D) With sternness

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's perfect balance of dignity and humility is a rare trait that indicates divine origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think about your own interactions: Do you treat people differently based on their social status? Where in your life do you show less respect to someone 'lower' than you, or more humility to someone 'higher'? What would it cost you to embody the prophetic balance—true dignity with the powerful and genuine humility with the weak—starting tomorrow?
?
The Prophet's trait was not a mask but his nature. Is your humility genuine or merely polite? And your dignity—is it pride or self-respect? Ask yourself: Which group—the worldly or the poor—do you find harder to treat with the prophetic balance? Why?
?
You claim to follow the Prophet, but does your treatment of the poor reflect his 'utmost humility'? If not, what is one concrete action you can take this week to honor the poor as he did, not out of pity but out of imaan?

Seventh Evidence: Forbearance Under Anger
Seventh evidence: forbearance under anger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's exceptional forbearance when angered serves as evidence of his prophethood.

Core Idea
Anger increased his forbearance, not his harshness.

The seventh evidence focuses on the Prophet's remarkable character, specifically his forbearance. When angered, which is when people most easily lose temper, he only became more gentle and forgiving. This lesson examines how such self-control is supernatural and points to divine support.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the description of his good character and its effect when angered.
Note the phrase 'لا يزداد مع الغضب إلا حلماً'.
2
Understand the paradox
Normally, anger increases harshness. The Prophet's anger increased his forbearance—a clear deviation from human nature.
This is a miracle of character.
3
Reflect on the implication
Such control is not humanly possible without divine assistance.
Thus it is a sign of prophethood.

Source Text

Eighth Evidence: Supernatural Beauty and Perfection
Eighth evidence: supernatural beauty and perfection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's unprecedented physical beauty and perfection serve as evidence of his prophethood.

Core Idea
His appearance itself was a miracle, unmatched in human history.

The eighth and final evidence from the Prophet's attributes is his extraordinary physical beauty and perfection, which were unprecedented. The passage includes a poetic testimony from a Companion and the historical example of Abu Dharr who embraced Islam upon seeing him. This lesson examines how even his appearance indicated truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the description of his beauty and the testimonies of Abdullah ibn Rawaha and Abu Dharr.
Note that his beauty is described as 'خرق عادة' (breach of custom).
2
Understand the testimonies
Abdullah ibn Rawaha said his appearance alone would inform of the truth. Abu Dharr embraced Islam just upon seeing him.
These are historical witnesses.
3
Reflect on the implication
If his appearance was so compelling that people believed without hearing his message, that itself is evidence.
This is a form of miracle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear that Abu Dharr believed simply by seeing the Prophet's face, do you feel a similar pull to faith? What might be blocking that response in your heart? How can you cultivate a longing to see the Prophet's beauty, even without physical sight?
?
If the Prophet's appearance was a miracle, why do you think you still doubt or waver in your faith? What does that reveal about your reliance on intellectual proofs versus sensory ones? Ask Allah to grant you certainty that transcends arguments.
?
Imagine standing before the Prophet today. Would his beauty move you to immediate obedience? If not, what must change in your life to prepare for that meeting? Make a concrete intention to study his physical description (shama'il) this week.

Prophethood

The Spiritual Proofs of Prophethood: Hardship, Humility, Character, and Beauty
Author enumerates four spiritual proofs of prophethood (5th to 8th) and concludes they are exclusive to prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand four spiritual proofs of prophethood and why they are considered exclusive to prophets.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unique endurance, humility, character, and beauty are spiritual proofs of his prophethood.

In this passage, Sanusi continues his list of spiritual proofs for prophethood, presenting four additional compelling evidences. These proofs are not physical miracles but rather the extraordinary moral and personal qualities of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). As you read, notice how each proof demonstrates a pattern of behavior that only a true prophet could sustain, and how the author supports them with historical anecdotes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the four enumerated proofs starting with 'وخامسها'.
Each proof begins with a number: fifth, sixth, seventh, eighth.
2
Examine each proof's logic
For each proof, ask: Why does this characteristic point to prophethood? For example, enduring hardships while persisting is beyond normal human capacity without divine support.
The proofs are cumulative and strengthen each other.
3
Consider the supporting anecdotes
Read the poetry of Ibn Rawāḥa and the story of Abū Dharr. How do these illustrate the proofs? They show that even the Prophet's appearance testified to his truthfulness.
These anecdotes are historical eyewitness accounts.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that these attributes, even individually, are not found in non-prophets. Why is this important for establishing the truth of his prophethood?
This conclusion ties all the proofs together as exclusive to prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخامسها : أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ تحمل في أداء الرسالة أنواعاً مِنَ المشاق والمتاعب لا يثبتُ معَها إلا مَنْ هو على الحقِّ مِنَ اللَّهِ تعالى ، وهو مع ذلكَ مصر على دعوى الرسالة ، ولم يظهر في عزمِهِ فتور ، ولا في إصراره قصور . وسادسُها : أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ كانَ معَ أهل الدنيا في غاية الترفعِ ، ومع الفقراء والمساكين في غاية التواضع . وسابعها : ما كانَ عليهِ مِنْ حسن الخلق ، حتى إنَّهُ لا يزدادُ معَ الغضب إلا حلماً . وثامنها : حسنُ ذاتِهِ الكريمة ، وما اشتملَتْ عليهِ مِنَ المحاسنِ التي هي خرقُ عادة ، ولم تُوجَدْ لبشر سواه . وما أحسن قول عبد الله بن رواحة الأنصاري رضي الله عنه في ذلكَ يشيرُ إلى محاسنِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ خَلْقاً وخُلقا : [ من البسيط] لو لم تَكُنْ فِيهِ آيَاتٌ مُبَيَّنَةٌ لَكَانَ مَنْظَرُهُ يُنْبِيكَ بِالْخَبَرِ . ولقد أسلم أبو ذر رضي الله عنه عندَ رؤيتِهِ إِيَّاهُ ، وقال : ( لا رأيْتُ وجهَهُ عرفْتُ أَنَّهُ ليسَ وجْهَ كَذَّاب ) . ولا خفاءَ أنَّ مجموعَ هذهِ الأوصاف بل بعضها لا يكون لغيرِ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام .
But the fifth: that he, peace be upon him, bore in delivering the message types of hardships and difficulties which only one who is upon the truth from Allah the Exalted can endure, and he was with that persistent in claiming the message, and no slackness appeared in his resolve, nor any shortcoming in his insistence. And the sixth: that he, peace be upon him, was with the people of the world in the utmost detachment, and with the poor and the needy in the utmost humility. And the seventh: his good character, such that he would not increase with anger except in forbearance. And the eighth: the goodness of his noble self, and what it contained of beauties that were a breach of custom, and were not found in any human other than him. And how excellent is the saying of ‘Abdullah ibn Rawāḥa al-Anṣārī, may Allah be pleased with him, referring to his beauties, peace be upon him, in form and character: [Basīṭ] 'If there were no clear signs in him, his appearance would inform you of the news.' And Abū Dharr, may Allah be pleased with him, embraced Islam upon seeing him, and said: 'I saw his face and knew that it is not the face of a liar.' And there is no hiddenness that the totality of these attributes, nay some of them, are not found in other than the prophets, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage lists four spiritual proofs (al-adilla al-'aqliyya) of prophethood, continuing a prior enumeration. The fifth proof is the Prophet's endurance of hardships in delivering the message while persisting unwaveringly. The sixth is his combination of detachment from worldly people and humility toward the poor. The seventh is his excellent character, which only became more forbearing with anger. The eighth is his physical beauty and perfect traits, which are a breach of custom (kharq al-‘āda) and unique to him. The author supports these with two anecdotes: the poetry of Ibn Rawāḥa, who says his appearance alone would inform of his truthfulness, and the conversion of Abū Dharr upon seeing his face. The passage concludes that these attributes, even individually, are exclusive to prophets.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The spiritual proofs like endurance, humility, good character, and physical beauty could be found in non-prophets as well.
Correction: The author asserts that these attributes, even individually, are not found in other than prophets. They are unique and serve as rational proofs of prophethood.

Key Takeaway
The four spiritual proofs—endurance, humility, character, and beauty—are unique to prophets and serve as rational evidence for prophethood.

?
The Prophet's beauty was so profound that Abū Dharr recognized truth at a glance. When others see you, do they see the reflection of prophetic character – forbearance in anger, honesty in speech? The Transmitted Proof of Prophethood
Author presents the transmitted proof (al-dalīl al-naqlī) of the Prophet's prophethood from earlier revelations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the testimony of earlier scriptures and prophets serves as a sufficient transmitted proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The testimony of established prophets is decisive proof of another's prophethood.

Sanusi now presents a second type of proof for prophethood: the transmitted proof from previous scriptures. He argues that the earlier prophets' testimony about Muhammad, preserved in their scriptures despite alteration, constitutes a sufficient proof in itself. This lesson examines that argument and its strength.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice the structure: definition, claim of sufficiency, evidence of mass transmission, and evidence of preservation.
2
Understand the nature of transmitted proof
This proof is based on Allah's text and the prophets' testimony, not on miracles. It is a 'naqli' (transmitted) proof.
Contrast with the previous proof (aqli) if covered earlier.
3
Examine the argument's strength
The author claims it is sufficient alone because a prophet's testimony is decisive. Consider why the testimony of an established prophet carries such weight.
Think about the credibility of prophets.
4
Note the evidence of preservation
Despite alterations, the prophethood text remains in the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms. This indicates divine care and frequent repetition that alteration cannot erase.
This strengthens the argument.
5
Reflect on the misconception
Some think transmitted proof is weaker than miracles. Sanusi says it is sufficient. How does this change your understanding?
This is the common misunderstanding addressed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النقلي : فهو نصُّهُ تعالى على نبوَّتِهِ في الكتب الماضية ، وذكر الأنبياء لهُ ، وإيصاؤُهُم على اتَّبَاعِهِ، وهذا الدليل وحده كافٍ بدونِ المعجزة ؛ فإنَّ شهادةَ مَنْ ثَبَتَتْ نبوَّتُهُ لأحد بالنبوة دليل قاطع على ثبوتِ نبيَّتِهِ وإِنْ لم تظهر معجزة على يده ، وقد تواترت عنِ الأحبار الأخبار عن كُتُبِهم وأنبيائهم بنبوته قبل مبعثِهِ مُعيَّنينَ اسْمَهُ وبلدَهُ وصفته ، وأيضاً فلم يزل نص نبوّتِهِ والحمد لله موجوداً في التوراة والإنجيل والزبورِ إلى الآنَ معَ مبالغتِهم في تبديلها ، وذلك يدلُّ على الاعتناء بأمرِهِ فيها ، وكثرة ترديد ذكره فيها على وجه لا يزيلُ جميعه التبديل
As for the transmitted proof: it is the text of Allah the Exalted concerning his prophethood in the previous scriptures, and the mention of him by the prophets, and their charge to follow him. And this proof alone is sufficient without a miracle, for the testimony of one whose prophethood is established to another's prophethood is a decisive proof of the establishment of his prophethood even if no miracle appears at his hand. And reports from the rabbis and their books and their prophets have been transmitted successively (mutawātir) concerning his prophethood before his mission, specifying his name, his land, and his description. Moreover, the text of his prophethood, praise be to Allah, has remained extant in the Torah, the Gospel, and the Psalms until now, despite their efforts to alter them. And that indicates attention to his matter in them, and the frequency of the repetition of his mention in them in a manner that alteration cannot remove all of it.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage presents the second category of proof, the transmitted proof (al-dalīl al-naqlī). It argues that the previous scriptures explicitly contain Allah's text affirming Muhammad's prophethood, and that earlier prophets mentioned him and commanded their followers to follow him. The author claims that this proof alone is sufficient, even without a miracle, because the testimony of an established prophet is decisive. He further asserts that reports from Jewish scholars (al-ahbār) and their scriptures have been mass-transmitted (tawātur) about his prophethood before his mission, specifying his name, land, and description. Finally, he notes that despite their efforts to alter the scriptures, the text of his prophethood has remained in the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms until the author's time, indicating divine care and frequent repetition that cannot be completely erased.

شهادة الأنبياء

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The transmitted proof from previous scriptures is weak and requires a miracle to be convincing.
Correction: Sanusi argues that the testimony of a prophet whose prophethood is established is decisive proof by itself, even without a miracle.
