[ تبشير الإنجيل ] وكذا قال المسيح في الإنجيل الذي بأيدي الكفرة اليوم : ( اللهم ؛ ابعثِ البَارِقْلِيطَ ليُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّ ابنَ الإِنسانِ بشرٌ ) وقال أيضاً في الإنجيل التي بأيديهم عن يُوحَنا : ( البَارِقْلِيطُ لا يجيئكم ما لم أذهب ، فإذا جاءَ وَبَّخَ العالم على الخطيئة ، ولا يقولُ مِنْ تلقاء نفسه شيئاً ، ولكنَّهُ ممَّا يسمعُ يُكلِّمكم ويسوسكم بالحقِّ ، ويخبركم بالحوادثِ والغيوب . . . ) إلى أنْ قالَ عنه : ( وسيعظُمُني ) ، ثم تمادى على وصفه بكلام بين ، وقال : ( هو يشهد لي كما شهدت له ، وأنا أجيتكم بالأمثال ، وهو يأتيكم بالتأويل ) . وفي الإنجيل أيضاً : ( أنَّ المسيحَ قالَ للحواريينَ : مَنْ أبغضني فقد أبغض الربَّ ) ، ثم تمادى إلى أنْ قالَ : ( فلا بدَّ أنْ تتمَّ الكلمةُ التي في الناموس ؛ لأنَّهم أبغضوني مجاناً ، فلو قد جاءَ المُنْحَمَنَّا الذي يرسلُهُ اللهُ إِليكم مِنْ عِندِ الربِّ روحِ القسط ، فهو شهيد عليَّ وأنتم أيضاً ، لكنكم قديماً كنتُم معي ، هذا قولي لكم لكيلا تشكُوا إذا جاءَ )
[Prophecy of the Gospel] And likewise said the Messiah in the Gospel that is in the hands of the disbelievers today: 'O God, send the Paraclete to inform the people that the Son of Man is a human.' And he also said in the Gospel that is in their hands according to John: 'The Paraclete will not come to you unless I go; when he comes, he will rebuke the world concerning sin, and he will not speak anything from himself, but he will speak to you from what he hears and will lead you in truth, and will inform you of events and hidden things...' until he said about him: 'And he will glorify me.' Then he continued describing him with clear speech, and said: 'He will bear witness to me just as I have borne witness to him, and I have come to you with parables, and he will bring you the interpretation.' And in the Gospel also: 'The Messiah said to the disciples: Whoever hates me has hated the Lord.' Then he continued until he said: 'It is necessary that the word in the Law be fulfilled, because they hated me without cause. So if the Munhamanna comes, whom God sends to you from the Lord, the Spirit of justice, he will be a witness about me and you also, but you were with me from the beginning. This I say to you so that you will not doubt when he comes.'
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage presents proof texts from the Gospel (Injil) interpreted as prophecies of Prophet Muhammad. The author first quotes a prayer of Jesus to send the Paraclete (al-Bāraqlīṭ) to teach people that the Son of Man is a human being – i.e., Jesus himself, affirming his humanity. Then a longer quote from the Gospel of John describes the Paraclete: he will not come until Jesus departs; he will rebuke the world of sin; he does not speak from himself but speaks what he hears; he will teach truth, inform of future events; he will glorify Jesus; he bears witness to Jesus as Jesus bore witness to him; Jesus brings parables, the Paraclete brings interpretation. Finally, a quote about the Munhamanna (a Syriac term for the Comforter, interpreted as Ahmad) sent from the Lord as the Spirit of truth, who will bear witness. The author uses these descriptions to argue that the Paraclete predicted in the Gospel is none other than Prophet Muhammad, who came after Jesus, taught from revelation, foretold future events, and brought the interpretation of the scriptures. This is a classic argument for Muhammad's prophethood from biblical prophecy.

Key Terms
البَارِقْلِيط
المُنْحَمَنَّا
الإنجيل
يُوحَنا
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Paraclete refers to the Holy Spirit.
Correction: Sanusi argues the Paraclete refers to a human prophet, Muhammad, based on the attributes in the Gospel: he speaks from hearing, brings interpretation, and is a human messenger.

Checkpoint
According to the Gospel quotes in the passage, what does the Paraclete NOT do?
A) Speak from himself
B) Speak what he hears
C) Glorify the Messiah
D) Inform of events

Key Takeaway
Sanusi uses Gospel passages to show that the Paraclete is a human prophet, identified as Muhammad, who would come after Jesus and bring full truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted the prophethood of Muhammad because you felt he came without prior announcement in earlier scriptures? How does this passage from the Gospel challenge that doubt? Will you commit to studying more biblical prophecies to strengthen your faith?
?
The Paraclete is described as one who brings truth and interpretation. In what areas of your life are you still relying on your own understanding rather than the revelation brought by the Prophet? What specific step will you take today to submit your intellect to the Qur’an and Sunnah?
?
Jesus said the Paraclete will glorify him. How do you glorify Jesus (as a prophet of Allah) in your daily actions? Does your life reflect that you accept Muhammad as the final messenger who clarified the truth about Jesus? Write one concrete change you will make this week.

Prophethood

The Paraclete Prophecy in the Gospel
Sanusi cites Jesus' prayer for the Paraclete and John's description of his role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the Gospel prophecy of the Paraclete to argue that Jesus is human and Muhammad is the promised prophet.

Core Idea
The Paraclete prophecy identifies Muhammad as the one who clarifies Jesus' humanity.

Sanusi begins by stating the purpose of Muhammad's mission: to inform people that Jesus is a human servant, not divine. He then cites Jesus' own prayer for the Paraclete and a detailed description from the Gospel of John, showing that the Paraclete is a human messenger who receives revelation and guides people in truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement and prayer
Read the first part where Sanusi states Muhammad's purpose and Jesus' prayer for the Paraclete. Notice that the prayer asks for a figure to inform people that the Son of Man is human.
This sets the stage for the entire argument.
2
Identify the Paraclete's roles in John
Read the longer passage from John. List the roles attributed to the Paraclete: he will not come until Jesus leaves, he will convict the world of sin, he will not speak on his own but only what he hears, he will guide in truth, announce unseen events, glorify Jesus, and bring interpretation.
These roles describe a prophetic figure, not a divine spirit.
3
Connect to Muhammad's mission
Sanusi is using these prophecies to show that the Paraclete is Muhammad. Consider how each role matches Muhammad's prophetic mission: receiving revelation, teaching truth, and clarifying Jesus' status.
This is a key step in the argument.
4
Reflect on the source
Notice that Sanusi uses the Gospel as preserved by Christians as evidence. This is a common approach in Islamic polemics: using the other scripture to prove Islam's claims.
It shows confidence in the original message of the Gospel.

وكاشفَ الغُمَّةِ نبيَّنا محمداً صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لِيُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّ عيسى عليه السلام بشر ، عبد الله تعالى ، وليسَ باله .
[ تبشير الإنجيل ]
وكذا قال المسيح في الإنجيل الذي بأيدي الكفرة اليوم : ( اللهم ؛ ابعثِ البَارِقْلِيطَ ليُعْلِمَ الناسَ أَنَّ ابنَ الإِنسانِ بشرٌ )
وقال أيضاً في الإنجيل التي بأيديهم عن يُوحَنا : ( البَارِقْلِيطُ لا يجيئكم ما لم أذهب ، فإذا جاءَ وَبَّخَ العالم على الخطيئة ، ولا يقولُ مِنْ تلقاء نفسه شيئاً ، ولكنَّهُ ممَّا يسمعُ يُكلِّمكم ويسوسكم بالحقِّ ، ويخبركم بالحوادثِ والغيوب . . . ) إلى أنْ قالَ عنه : ( وسيعظُمُني ) ، ثم تمادى على وصفه بكلام بين ، وقال : ( هو يشهد لي كما شهدت له ، وأنا أجيتكم بالأمثال ، وهو يأتيكم بالتأويل ) . وفي الإنجيل أيضاً : ( أنَّ المسيحَ قالَ للحواريينَ : مَنْ أبغضني فقد أبغض الربَّ ) ، ثم تمادى إلى أنْ قالَ : ( فلا بدَّ أنْ تتمَّ الكلمةُ التي في الناموس ؛ لأنَّهم أبغضوني مجاناً ، فلو قد جاءَ المُنْحَمَنَّا الذي يرسلُهُ اللهُ إِليكم مِنْ عِندِ الربِّ روحِ القسط ، فهو شهيد عليَّ وأنتم أيضاً ، لكنكم قديماً كنتُم معي ، هذا قولي لكم لكيلا تشكُوا إذا جاءَ )
والمُنْحَمَنَّا : بلسانِ السُّريانية وهو بالرومية : البارقليط وبالعربية : محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ .
وفي الإنجيل أيضاً عن المسيح : أنه ضرب مثلاً للدنيا فقال : ( مثلُ الدنيا كمثلِ رجل اغترسَ كَرْماً ومضى على ذلك ) ، ثم ضربَ مثلاً للأنبياء ولنفسِهِ في كلام كثيرٍ ، ثم لمحمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وجعله الموكل آخراً بالكَرْمَ ، وأفصح عن أُمَّةِ محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فقال : ( أقولُ : إِنَّهُ سَيُزاح عنكم مُلكُ الله تعالى ، وتُعطاهُ الأمةُ المطيعة العاملة ) ، ثم ضرب مثلاً بصخرة وقال : ( مَنْ سقط على هذهِ الصخرة سينكسرُ ، ومَنْ سقطَتْ عليه سيتهشم ) ؛ يريد بذلك : محمداً صلَّى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ ؛ مَنْ ناواه وحاربه أظهرَهُ اللهُ عليهِ .
And the remover of distress, our Prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, so that he might inform the people that Jesus, peace be upon him, is a human, a servant of God Almighty, and not a god. [Evangelization of the Gospel] Likewise, the Messiah said in the Gospel that is in the hands of the disbelievers today: 'O God, send the Paraclete to inform the people that the Son of Man is a human.' And he also said in the Gospel that is in their hands, according to John: 'The Paraclete will not come to you unless I go; when he comes, he will convict the world concerning sin, and he will not speak on his own authority, but whatever he hears he will speak, and he will guide you in truth, and will tell you of events and unseen things...' until he said about him: 'And he will glorify me.' Then he continued describing him with clear speech, and said: 'He will testify for me as I have testified for him, and I come to you with parables, and he will come to you with interpretation.' And in the Gospel also: 'The Messiah said to the disciples: Whoever hates me has hated the Lord.' Then he continued until he said: 'But the word that is in the Law must be fulfilled: They hated me without a cause. When the Munhamanna comes, whom God will send to you from the Lord, the Spirit of justice, he will be a witness for me, and you also, but you have been with me from the beginning; this I say to you so that you may not doubt when he comes.' And al-Munhamanna: in Syriac, and in Greek it is al-Barqalit (Paraclete), and in Arabic: Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. And in the Gospel also, from the Messiah: that he gave a parable of the world, saying: 'The parable of the world is like a man who planted a vineyard and went on...' Then he gave a parable of the prophets and of himself in much speech, then of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, and made him the last entrusted with the vineyard, and he spoke clearly about the nation of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, saying: 'I say: The kingdom of God will be taken away from you and given to an obedient, working nation.' Then he gave a parable of a rock and said: 'Whoever falls on this rock will be broken, and whoever it falls on will be crushed'; meaning by that Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace; whoever opposes him and fights him, God will give him victory over him.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage is a proof from previous scriptures (the Gospel) for the prophethood of Muhammad. The author first states the purpose: Muhammad was sent to clarify that Jesus is a human servant, not divine. Then he cites specific Gospel passages, as preserved in the hands of Christians, that foretell the coming of a figure called the Paraclete (al-Barqalit) or al-Munhamanna. The author interprets these prophecies as referring to Muhammad. He quotes Jesus' prayer for the Paraclete to inform people that the Son of Man is human. Then a longer passage from John describes the Paraclete's role: he will not come until Jesus departs, will convict the world of sin, speak not from himself but from what he hears, guide in truth, and announce future events. Jesus says the Paraclete will glorify him and bring interpretation after Jesus brought parables. Another passage speaks of hatred towards Jesus, and the coming of al-Munhamanna (identified as the Spirit of justice) who will be a witness. The author then clarifies that al-Munhamanna is Syriac, corresponding to Greek Paraclete, and Arabic Muhammad. Next, he cites a parable of a vineyard: a man planted a vineyard, then sent various prophets, and finally sent Muhammad as the one entrusted with it, and the rule would be given to an obedient nation. Another parable of a rock refers to Muhammad: whoever opposes him will be broken. The passage thus uses Christian scripture to argue that Muhammad is the promised prophet.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Paraclete is a divine spirit or the Holy Spirit.
Correction: The Gospel description shows the Paraclete is a human prophet who does not speak on his own but receives revelation, and Jesus prayed for him to clarify that Jesus is human.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the purpose of the Paraclete's coming as stated in Jesus' prayer?
A) To judge the world
B) To inform people that the Son of Man is human
C) To bring peace
D) To establish a new law

Key Takeaway
The Gospel of John contains a prophecy of a figure called the Paraclete who will reveal the truth about Jesus and guide people in truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your heart, do you truly accept that Jesus (peace be upon him) is a servant and not a god, as the Paraclete came to clarify? Or do you harbor subtle doubts that elevate him beyond his prophetic station? What specific action can you take today to honor Jesus as a human prophet sent to his people?
?
The Paraclete is said to guide people in truth and not speak from himself. When you hear the Qur'an recited, do you receive it as if it is not from the messenger but from the One who sent him? Or do you treat it as mere human words? Commit to one verse today and reflect on its divine origin as if you are hearing it for the first time.
?
If the Gospel itself contains a prophecy about Muhammad (peace be upon him), how does that affect your view of the People of the Book? Will you engage with them with the truth of Islam, or do you avoid such conversations? This week, consider how you can share the message of the Paraclete's true identity with one Christian acquaintance, even if only through dua.

Prophethood

Al-Munhamanna: The Gospel Name of Muhammad
Sanusi identifies al-Munhamanna as Muhammad and explains vineyard and rock parables.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi identifies al-Munhamanna with Muhammad and interprets the parables of the vineyard and the rock as prophecies of his mission.

Core Idea
The Gospel names Muhammad as al-Munhamanna, and parables confirm his role as the final victorious prophet.

Sanusi continues by citing another Gospel prophecy that explicitly mentions a figure called al-Munhamanna, whom he identifies as Muhammad in Arabic. He then presents two parables from Jesus: the vineyard parable, which shows Muhammad as the final messenger entrusted with God's kingdom, and the rock parable, which symbolizes the inevitable victory of those who oppose him. This lesson unpacks these prophetic evidences.

Guided Path
1
Read the al-Munhamanna prophecy
Read the passage where Jesus prophesies about al-Munhamanna after warning about hatred. Note that al-Munhamanna is described as a witness and the Spirit of justice.
This prophecy is from the Gospel but not from the canonical books exactly; it is cited as found in the hands of Christians.
2
Understand the identification
Sanusi explicitly states that al-Munhamanna in Syriac is the Paraclete in Greek and Muhammad in Arabic. This is the direct claim that the Gospel predicts Muhammad by name.
This equivalence is central to the argument.
3
Examine the vineyard parable
Read the parable of the vineyard. The man (God) plants a vineyard (the world/religion), sends various prophets, and finally sends Muhammad as the last entrusted one. The kingdom is then given to an obedient nation (the Muslim community).
This parable shows a succession of prophets culminating in Muhammad.
4
Examine the rock parable
Read the parable of the rock. The rock is Muhammad; whoever falls on it (opposes him) will be broken; whoever it falls on will be crushed. This symbolizes the victory of Muhammad over his enemies.
The interpretation is given explicitly in the text.
5
Reflect on cumulative evidence
Consider how multiple Gospel passages (the Paraclete, al-Munhamanna, the parables) all point to Muhammad as the promised prophet. This builds a strong case from within Christian scripture.
This is a classic Islamic argument for the prophethood of Muhammad.

Next, he cites a parable of a vineyard: a man planted a vineyard, then sent various prophets, and finally sent Muhammad as the one entrusted with it, and the rule would be given to an obedient nation. Another parable of a rock refers to Muhammad: whoever opposes him will be broken. The passage thus uses Christian scripture to argue that Muhammad is the promised prophet.

Sanusi cites Isaiah's prophecy describing Muhammad's characteristics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses a prophecy from Isaiah to foretell the coming of Prophet Muhammad and the key characteristics mentioned.

Core Idea
Isaiah's prophecy describes Muhammad by name and character — a proof from earlier scripture.

Sanusi presents a prophecy from the biblical prophet Isaiah that he interprets as referring to the coming of Muhammad. The passage includes descriptions of a servant of God who will receive revelation, open blind eyes and deaf ears, and be called Ahmad. This lesson examines how this prophecy is presented as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood from previous scriptures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the prophecy's own rhythm come through before interpreting.
Note that the passage ends abruptly; the full context is not given.
2
Identify the attributes of the servant
The passage describes a servant who receives revelation, does not laugh loudly, opens blind eyes and sealed hearts, and is named Ahmad. List these attributes and consider how they match Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Ahmad is another name of the Prophet Muhammad.
3
Understand the significance of this prophecy
This prophecy is taken from the Bible (Isaiah) and is used to show that Muhammad's coming was foretold in earlier scriptures, strengthening the case for his prophethood.
Consider the interfaith dimension of this evidence.

[Evangelization of Isaiah, peace be upon him] And the prophet Isaiah said from God Almighty: 'My servant in whom my soul delights, I will send down my revelation upon him, so that he will manifest my justice among the nations, he will command the nations with the commandments, he does not laugh, nor is his voice heard in the markets, he opens blind eyes, sealed hearts, and what I give him I do not give to others, he makes deaf ears hear, and gives life to others, Ahmed praises God with praise.' Then he pointed to his country, Mecca, and said: 'The wilderness will rejoice, and its inhabitants will say 'La ilaha illa Allah' (there is no god but God) on every hill, and magnify Him (say 'Allahu Akbar') on every mound, he does not weaken nor is he overcome, nor does he incline to whim, nor is his voice heard in the markets, nor will he be humiliated.'
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage presents a prophecy from Isaiah (a biblical prophet) that the author interprets as foretelling Muhammad. The prophecy is presented as God speaking: 'My servant in whom my soul delights' – this servant is one upon whom God will send revelation, and he will manifest divine justice among the nations. The description includes that he does not laugh loudly, nor is his voice raised in markets (implying modesty and dignity). He will open blind eyes and sealed hearts (metaphorically, guiding people), and he will make the deaf hear and give life (spiritual life). The name 'Ahmed' appears: 'Ahmed praises God with praise' – Ahmed is another name of Muhammad. Then the prophecy shifts to describing the land of this prophet: the wilderness (Mecca and its surroundings) will rejoice, and its people will glorify God on every elevated place, saying 'Allahu Akbar' (God is greatest). The servant will not be weak or defeated, nor will he follow his desires, nor will his voice be raised in markets, and he will not be humiliated. The passage is cut off but clearly identifies Muhammad as the promised servant from Isaiah.

Correction: Sanusi interprets the prophecy specifically for Muhammad, citing the name Ahmad and the description of the land (Mecca), which aligns with Islamic tradition.

Gospel Prophecy of the Paraclete: Muhammad in the Bible
Identifies the Paraclete as Muhammad and cites Gospel parables.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic scholars interpret Gospel references to the Paraclete and the parable of the vineyard as prophecies of Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Greek 'Paraclete' is Muhammad, foretold in the Gospel.

Sanusi cites proofs from the Gospel to establish the prophethood of Muhammad. He identifies the Paraclete—called al-Munhamanna in Syriac and al-Baraqlit in Greek—as Muhammad in Arabic. He then interprets Jesus' parables of the vineyard and the rock as clear references to the final Prophet. This passage demonstrates that the Bible itself foretold the coming of Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms for the Paraclete in three languages.
2
Identify the Paraclete identification
The author directly states that al-Munhamanna (Syriac) = al-Baraqlit (Greek) = Muhammad (Arabic). This is a bold claim that the biblical figure is the Prophet Muhammad.
The term 'Paraclete' in the Gospel of John is usually translated as 'Comforter' or 'Holy Spirit' in Christian tradition.
3
Analyze the vineyard parable
Jesus compares the world to a vineyard, the prophets to workers, and finally entrusts it to Muhammad. This suggests Muhammad is the final authority.
The parable echoes the concept of stewardship in the Bible.
4
Understand the rock parable and its implication
The rock represents Muhammad: those who oppose him will be broken, but those whom it falls on will be crushed. This signifies that opposing Muhammad leads to destruction, while accepting him is safe.

Isaiah's Prophecy of Muhammad
Isaiah's prophecy is cited and interpreted as foretelling Muhammad's universal mission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophecy from Isaiah is interpreted as foretelling Muhammad's universal mission, and how it contrasts with Jesus's mission.

Core Idea
Isaiah's prophecy of a universal servant points to Muhammad, not Jesus.

In this passage, the author presents a biblical prophecy from Isaiah as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood. The prophecy describes a servant who will command all nations, bring justice, and be a light. The author then contrasts this with Jesus's own words in the Gospel that he was sent only to Israel. This comparison argues that the universal messenger must be Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the prophecy and commentary

Jesus said he was sent only to Israel, but Isaiah's servant commands all nations.

This shows an interfaith argument using previous scriptures.

Proof from Torah and Gospel that Muhammad is the Universal Prophet

The Torah and Gospel both point to Muhammad as the prophet for all nations.

The author presents a proof from the Torah and Gospel, demonstrating that Muhammad is the universal prophet. He cites two testimonies: one from the Torah about a prophet who will command the nations, and one from the Gospel where Jesus says he was sent only to Israel. This leaves Muhammad as the only possible candidate for a universal mission.

Guided Path

Read the passage carefully

The passage is compact; each part builds toward the conclusion.

The passage quotes a Torah statement ('He commands the nations') and a Gospel statement (Jesus saying he was sent only to the lost sheep of Israel). Identify each and note their sources.
3
Understand the logical conclusion

This is a classic argument from earlier scriptures.
4
Reflect on the significance

Commentary
This passage provides a proof of prophethood by citing earlier scriptures. The author first mentions that the truth submits to the Torah, then calls attention to a clear statement about Muhammad from multiple sources. He cites two examples: one from the Torah (God's saying "He commands the nations") and one from the Gospel (Jesus saying he was only sent to the lost sheep of Israel). From this, the author concludes that Jesus cannot be the universal prophet, so the one sent to all nations must be Muhammad. This is a classic argument in polemics.

Key Terms
توراة
إنجيل
تصريح
الأمم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jesus was sent to all nations as a universal prophet.
Correction: The Gospel shows Jesus saying he was sent only to the lost sheep of Israel, so his mission was limited, not universal.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why cannot Jesus be the prophet sent to all nations?
A) Because Jesus said he was not sent to all races, only to the lost sheep of Israel.
B) Because Jesus was not mentioned in the Torah.
C) Because the Torah commands the nations.
D) Because Muhammad is the only prophet mentioned in the Gospel.

Key Takeaway
The Torah and Gospel both indicate that Muhammad is the universal prophet, while Jesus's mission was limited to Israel.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Torah and Gospel point to Muhammad as the universal prophet. Does your faith in Muhammad rest on such evidence from earlier scriptures, or only on the Quran? If you are honest, have you ever truly examined the Bible for signs of Islam? What would it cost you to do so this week?
?
Jesus said he was sent only to the lost sheep of Israel. Does that make you uneasy about any previous assumptions you held about Jesus? How does this affect your understanding of God's plan for humanity? Ask yourself: Am I willing to let this scriptural testimony reshape my view of prophethood, even if it challenges popular narratives?
?
The author says 'the truth submits to His Torah.' Do you truly believe that all truth, even from non-Muslim sources, ultimately submits to God? Are you open to finding truth in unexpected places, or do you only accept what you already know? Examine your heart: Are you willing to submit to truth wherever it appears, even if it means changing long-held beliefs?

First prophecy from Isaiah: The desert rejoices with Ahmad
Isaiah prophesies that the desert will be given the beauties of Lebanon through Ahmad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophecy from Isaiah about the desert rejoicing is interpreted as referring to Prophet Muhammad (Ahmad).

Core Idea
The Bible foretold the coming of Ahmad with blessings.

In this lesson, we examine the first of three prophecies cited from the book of Isaiah. It speaks of the desert rejoicing because it will be given the beauties of Lebanon—a reference to the blessings brought by Ahmad, understood as a name of Prophet Muhammad. This passage is part of a larger tradition that finds references to the Prophet in earlier scriptures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the key term 'Ahmad' and the imagery of the desert and Lebanon.
The passage is a direct quote from the scriptures of Isaiah.
2
Identify the subject of the prophecy
Ask: Who is 'Ahmad'? The author identifies him with Prophet Muhammad. Consider why the desert is said to rejoice.
Ahmad is a name of the Prophet mentioned in the Quran (Surah As-Saff 61:6).
3
Reflect on the interpretation
Think about how this prophecy is used as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood. What does the beauties of Lebanon symbolize?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي صحف إشعياء : ( لتفرح أرضُ البادية العطشى ، ولتبتهج البراري والفلواتُ ؛ لأنَّها ستعطى بأحمد محاسن لبنان ، وكمثل حسن الدساكر والرياض ((١) وفي صحف إشعياء أيضاً : ( أَتَتْ أيام الافتقادِ ، أَتَتْ أيامُ الكمال ) ، ثم قال : ( لتعلموا يا بني إسرائيل الجاهلين : أنَّ الذي تُسمُّونَهُ ضالاً هو صاحبُ النبوَّةِ ، تفترونَ ذلك على كثرة ذنوبكم وعظم فجوركم ((٢) وفي صحفِ إشعياء أيضاً يقول : ( قيل لي : قُمْ ناظراً ، فما ترى تخبر بهِ ، قلتُ : أرى راكبين مقبلين ؛ أحدهما على حمارٍ ، والآخرُ على جمل، يقول أحدهما لصاحبِهِ : سقطَتْ بابل وأصنامها النخرة ) ؛ فصاحب الجمل : هو نبينا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، كما أنَّ صاحب الحمار هو عيسى عليه السلام ، مشهورين بذلك وإِنَّما سقطَتْ عبادة الأصنام ببابلَ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ وهُدَّتْ أوثانُها .. بنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ علَيهِ وسلَّمَ وأَمَّتِهِ ، لا بعيسى عليه السلام ولا بغيره ، فما زالَتْ ملوك بابل يعبدون الأصنامَ مِنْ لدن إبراهيم إلى زمان نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وأَمَّتِهِ (٣)
And in the scriptures of Isaiah: 'Let the thirsty desert land rejoice, and let the deserts and wastelands be glad; for it shall be given to Ahmad the beauties of Lebanon, and like the beauty of the towns and meadows.' (1) And also in the scriptures of Isaiah: 'The days of visitation have come, the days of perfection have come.' Then he said: 'So know, O ignorant children of Israel, that the one you call misguided is the possessor of prophethood; you invent that because of your many sins and great wickedness.' (2) And in the scriptures of Isaiah he also says: 'It was said to me: Stand up and look, and tell what you see. I said: I see two riders approaching; one on a donkey and the other on a camel. One says to his companion: Babylon has fallen, and its rotten idols.' So the rider on the camel is our Prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, just as the rider on the donkey is Jesus, peace be upon them, well-known for that. And indeed the worship of idols in Babylon fell, and its idols were destroyed, only by our Prophet and Master Muhammad and his community, not by Jesus nor anyone else. For the kings of Babylon continued to worship idols from the time of Abraham until the time of our Prophet and Master Muhammad and his community. (3)
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage presents three prophecies from the book of Isaiah that the author interprets as referring to Prophet Muhammad. The first speaks of the desert rejoicing because it will be given the beauties of Lebanon in connection with Ahmad. The second warns Israel that the one they consider misguided is actually the prophet. The third describes two riders: one on a donkey (Jesus) and one on a camel (Muhammad), and the fall of Babylon's idols is attributed to Muhammad's community. The author explicitly identifies the camel rider as Muhammad and notes that the fall of idolatry in Babylon occurred through Muhammad and his ummah, not through Jesus.

Second prophecy from Isaiah: The possessor of prophethood
Isaiah announces days of visitation and rebukes Israel for calling the prophet misguided.

Learning Objective

The second prophecy from Isaiah is a warning to the children of Israel. It announces the days of visitation and perfection, and then rebukes them for considering the prophet to be misguided. Third prophecy from Isaiah: The rider on the camel
Isaiah's vision of two riders (donkey and camel) interpreted as Jesus and Muhammad, with fall of Babylon's idols attributed to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third prophecy from Isaiah about two riders (donkey and camel) and how the camel rider is interpreted as Muhammad, and the fall of Babylon's idols through his mission.

Core Idea
Isaiah's vision of two riders points to Jesus and Muhammad, and the fall of idols in Babylon is by Muhammad.

The third prophecy from Isaiah describes a vision of two riders—one on a donkey and one on a camel. The author identifies the donkey rider as Jesus and the camel rider as Muhammad. He then explains that the fall of idolatry in Babylon, which lasted from Abraham until Muhammad, was accomplished by Muhammad and his community, not by Jesus. This is a key argument for Muhammad's prophethood from the Bible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the narrative: the prophet is told to stand and look, sees two riders, and hears that Babylon has fallen.
The riders are explicitly identified later.
2
Identify the riders
Find where the author says the rider on the camel is Muhammad and the rider on the donkey is Jesus. Compare with historical context.
The donkey is associated with Jesus' entry into Jerusalem; the camel is associated with Arabia.
3
Understand the claim about Babylon
The author asserts that the destruction of idols in Babylon happened through Muhammad and his ummah, not through Jesus. Consider why this is significant.
Babylon (Iraq) remained a center of idolatry until the Islamic conquests.
4
Reflect on the argument
Think about how this prophecy is used as proof that Muhammad is the expected prophet, and that his mission fulfilled what was foretold.

Isaiah's prophecies foretell Muhammad by name and sign.

Sanusi turns to the Bible to demonstrate that the coming of Prophet Muhammad was announced in previous scriptures. 4

وفي صحف إشعياء : ( لتفرح أرضُ البادية العطشى ، ولتبتهج البراري والفلواتُ ؛ لأنَّها ستعطى بأحمد محاسن لبنان ، وكمثل حسن الدساكر والرياض ((1) وفي صحف إشعياء أيضاً : ( أَتَتْ أيام الافتقادِ ، أَتَتْ أيامُ الكمال ) ، ثم قال : ( لتعلموا يا بني إسرائيل الجاهلين : أنَّ الذي تُسمُّونَهُ ضالاً هو صاحبُ النبوَّةِ ، تفترونَ ذلك على كثرة ذنوبكم وعظم فجوركم ((2) وفي صحفِ إشعياء أيضاً يقولُ : ( قيل لي : قُمْ ناظراً ، فما ترى تخبر بهِ ، قلتُ : أرى راكبين مقبلين ؛ أحدهما على حمارٍ ، والآخرُ على جمل، يقول أحدهما لصاحبِهِ : سقطَتْ بابل وأصنامها النخرة ) (3) ; فصاحب الجمل : هو نبينا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، كما أنَّ صاحب الحمار هو عيسى عليه السلام ، مشهورين بذلك وإِنَّما سقطَتْ عبادة الأصنام ببابلَ مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ وهُدَّتْ أوثانُها .. بنبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ علَيهِ وسلَّمَ وأَمَّتِهِ ، لا بعيسى عليه السلام ولا بغيره ، فما زالَتْ ملوك بابل يعبدون الأصنامَ مِنْ لدن إبراهيم إلى زمان نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وأَمَّتِهِ
And in the scriptures of Isaiah: 'Let the thirsty desert land rejoice, and let the wilderness and plains be glad; for they will be given by Ahmad the beauties of Lebanon, and like the beauty of towns and gardens.' And in the scriptures of Isaiah also: 'The days of visitation have come, the days of perfection have come.' Then he said: 'Let you know, O ignorant Children of Israel, that the one you call misguided is the owner of prophethood; you invent that due to the abundance of your sins and the greatness of your wickedness.' And in the scriptures of Isaiah also he says: 'It was said to me: Arise, look, and what you see you shall report. I said: I see two riders approaching; one on a donkey, and the other on a camel. One says to his companion: Babylon and its decaying idols have fallen.' So the rider on the camel is our Prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, just as the rider on the donkey is Jesus, peace be upon them both, well-known for that. Indeed, the worship of idols in Babylon besides God fell and its idols were demolished by our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, and his community, not by Jesus, peace be upon him, nor by anyone else. For the kings of Babylon continued to worship idols from the time of Abraham until the time of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, and his community.
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage presents three prophecies from the book of Isaiah that Sanusi interprets as glad tidings of the coming of Prophet Muhammad. The first prophecy speaks of the desert land rejoicing because it will be given 'by Ahmad' the beauties of Lebanon. 'Ahmad' is one of the names of the Prophet Muhammad, and the desert land is interpreted as Arabia. The second prophecy announces the arrival of 'days of visitation and perfection,' and identifies the one considered misguided by the Children of Israel as the true prophet. The third prophecy describes a vision of two riders: one on a donkey (Jesus) and one on a camel (Muhammad), who announces the fall of Babylon's idols. Sanusi explains that the destruction of idol worship in Babylon was accomplished by the Prophet Muhammad and his community, not by Jesus, as the Babylonian kings continued idolatry up to the time of Islam. The passage thus demonstrates that earlier scriptures foretold Muhammad's mission and the triumph of monotheism through him.

إشعياء
أحمد
صاحب الجمل
صاحب الحمار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The rider on the donkey in Isaiah's prophecy is Muhammad.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies the rider on the donkey is Jesus, while the rider on the camel is Muhammad.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's interpretation of the Isaiah prophecy about two riders, who is the rider on the camel?
A) Jesus
B) Muhammad
C) Abraham
D) Moses

Key Takeaway
Sanusi demonstrates that the book of Isaiah contains clear prophecies about the coming of Muhammad and the triumph of monotheism through him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Bible passage says the prophet was called 'misguided' by his own people. Have you ever dismissed someone who brings you truth simply because they did not fit your expectations? What would it take for you to recognize a true message from Allah even if it comes from an unexpected source?
?
The prophecy promises that the desert land will rejoice because it will be given 'by Ahmad the beauties of Lebanon.' Your life before guidance was like a barren desert. What 'beauties' has the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) brought into your life that you now take for granted? Will you thank Allah and send salawat upon him right now?
?
The fall of Babylon’s idols happened because of Muhammad and his community. What idols—whether pride, comfort, reputation, or desires—are still standing in your heart? Are you willing to let them fall, even if it costs you everything you have built, just as the Babylonian kings had to surrender their ancient worship?

Glad Tidings of Prophet Muhammad in Ezekiel
Sanusi interprets Ezekiel's vine parable as a prophecy of Muhammad's mission in Mecca.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets Ezekiel's vine parable as a prophecy of Muhammad's mission in Mecca, and how the descriptions of the land point to Mecca.

Core Idea
Ezekiel's prophecy points to Muhammad in Mecca.

In this passage, Sanusi draws from the scriptures of Ezekiel to show that the coming of Prophet Muhammad was foretold in the Bible. He focuses on a parable of a vine that is uprooted and replaced by a new plant in a desert, neglected land. This new plant, Sanusi argues, represents the prophetic mission of Muhammad in Mecca. Let's read the text and unpack the interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the key descriptions of the land.
Focus on the words for neglected, desert, thirsty.
2
Identify the elements of the prophecy
Identify the old vine (Children of Israel), the new plant (Muhammad's mission), and the land (Mecca). See how Sanusi connects them.
3
Understand Sanusi's reasoning
Ask yourself why Sanusi says the description matches Mecca. Consider the spiritual and physical state of Mecca before Islam.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي صحف حزقيال النبي يقولُ عن اللهِ عزَّ وجلَّ بعد ما ذكرَ معاصي بني إسرائيل وشبَّهَهم بكَرْمَةِ وقال : ( لم تلبث تلكَ الكَرْمَةُ أنْ قلِعَتْ بالسخطة ، ورُمِيَ بها على الأرضِ ، وأحرقَتِ السمائمُ ثمارها (1) ، فعند ذلكَ غُرِسَ غرسُ في البدو ، وفي الأرض المهملة العطشى ، وخرجَتْ مِنْ أغصانِها الفاضلة نارٌ أكلَتْ تلكَ الكَرْمَةَ ، حتى لم يُوجَدْ فيها غصن قوي ولا قضيب ) (2) فاعتبر هذا التصريح بهِ وبصفة بلدِهِ كلَّها ، وقوله : ( الأرض المهملة ، البدو ، العطشى ( ، وتلك صفاتُ مكَّةَ ؛ لأنَّها صحراء ، ولأنَّها كانَتْ مهملةً مِنَ النبوَّةِ مِنْ عهدِ إسماعيل عليه السلام .
And in the scriptures of the Prophet Ezekiel, he says about God Almighty after he mentioned the sins of the Children of Israel and likened them to a vine, and said: 'That vine did not last long; it was uprooted in wrath, thrown to the ground, and the hot winds burned its fruits. Then at that time a plant was planted in the desert, in the neglected and thirsty land, and from its excellent branches a fire came out that ate that vine, until no strong branch or twig was found in it.' So consider this clear statement about him and about the description of his land entirely, and his saying: 'the neglected land, the desert, the thirsty' – and those are descriptions of Mecca; because it is a desert, and because it was neglected from prophethood since the time of Ishmael, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage presents a prophecy from the book of Ezekiel. Sanusi explains that Ezekiel describes how God, after punishing the Children of Israel (likened to a vine that is uprooted and burned), plants a new shoot in a desert, neglected, and thirsty land. The new shoot represents the prophetic mission of Muhammad in Mecca, which was a barren desert and had not received a prophet since Ishmael. The fire from its branches that consumes the old vine symbolizes the spread of Islam that overcame earlier corruption. Sanusi directs the reader to note the explicit description of the land as 'neglected, desert, thirsty,' which matches the physical and spiritual state of Mecca before Islam. Thus, Ezekiel's prophecy is interpreted as a clear prediction of the coming of Muhammad and the rise of Islam in Mecca.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the vine represents all nations or a generic parable.
Correction: Sanusi specifies that the vine is about Israel, and the new plant is specifically Muhammad's mission in Mecca, as indicated by the descriptions of the land.

Checkpoint

A) Babylon
B) Medina
C) Mecca
D) Jerusalem

Key Takeaway
Sanusi interprets Ezekiel's prophecy as a clear prediction of Muhammad's prophetic mission in Mecca, based on the description of the land as neglected, desert, and thirsty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Ezekiel's prophecy was preserved and used by Sanusi to confirm Muhammad's mission. Is your belief in Muhammad built on such solid evidence, or is it borrowed from culture? Commit to one action this week to strengthen your conviction through the proofs given in this lesson.

Glad Tidings of Prophet Muhammad in Daniel
Sanusi uses Daniel's prophecy to argue that Muhammad's enduring call proves his prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a prophecy in the book of Daniel is used to confirm the truthfulness of Prophet Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
A false prophet's mission cannot last, but Muhammad's has endured for centuries.

In this passage, Sanusi invokes the prophecy of Daniel to distinguish true prophethood from false claims. He argues that because false claimants cannot maintain a call beyond thirty years, the remarkable longevity of Muhammad's message—nearly nine hundred years at the time of writing—stands as clear evidence of its divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic text and its English translation carefully. Notice the structure: a quote from Daniel followed by Sanusi's commentary.
2
Understand the prophecy
Identify the key claim: false prophets' calls do not last more than thirty years. Why is this significant?
The prophecy sets a criterion for distinguishing truth from falsehood.
3
Apply to Muhammad
Sanusi then applies this criterion to Prophet Muhammad: his call has lasted nearly 900 years and will continue until the Day of Resurrection. What does this imply?
4
Reflect on the argument
Consider how this argument from prophecy strengthens the case for Muhammad's truthfulness. What does it say about the nature of divine missions?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي صحفِ دانيال النبي عليهِ السلامُ وقد نعت الكذَّابينَ وقالَ : ) لا تمتد دعوتُهم ، ولا يتمُّ قُربانهم ، وأقسم الربُّ بساعده لا يظهرُ الباطل ولا يقومُ لمدَّعِ كاذب دعوة أكثرَ مِنْ ثلاثين سنة )(3) فاعتبر من هذا الكلام عدم طول دعوة الكذابينَ ، وهذه دعوة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قائمةٌ ظاهرة قريباً مِنْ تسع مئة سنة ، وهي باقية إلى يوم القيامة .
And in the scriptures of the Prophet Daniel, peace be upon him, when he described the liars and said: 'Their call will not extend, nor will their offering be completed, and the Lord swore by His arm that falsehood will not appear, nor will a false claimant have a call lasting more than thirty years.' So consider from this speech the lack of length of the call of liars. And this call of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, is established and manifest for nearly nine hundred years, and it will remain until the Day of Resurrection.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage presents a prophecy from the book of Daniel. Sanusi quotes Daniel as stating that false claimants to prophethood will not have a call lasting more than thirty years. Sanusi then points out that the call of Prophet Muhammad has already endured nearly nine hundred years (from the time of writing) and will continue until the Day of Resurrection. This serves as evidence of Muhammad's truthfulness: if he were a false prophet, his mission would have perished within a few decades, but instead it has lasted for centuries and continues to thrive. Thus, Daniel's prophecy is used to distinguish the true prophet from false ones by the longevity and persistence of his message.

Key Terms
دانيال
الكذابون
دعوة
ثلاثين سنة
تسع مئة سنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Daniel's prophecy is about the lifespan of each false prophet individually.
Correction: Sanusi interprets the prophecy as referring to the duration of the false claimant's prophetic mission or religion, not the person's life.

Checkpoint
How does Sanusi use Daniel's prophecy to prove that Muhammad is a true prophet?
A) Daniel said a true prophet will appear after 30 years
B) Daniel said false claimants' calls last at most 30 years, but Muhammad's call has lasted nearly 900 years
C) Daniel said the false prophet will be killed after 30 years
D) Daniel said the true prophet will be from Mecca

Key Takeaway
The enduring success of Muhammad's message, despite Daniel's prophecy limiting false calls, confirms his true prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Sanusi points to nearly 900 years of success as proof. Your life is only a few decades long—are you investing those years in a call that will last forever, or in something that will fade within 30 years? What will you do today to shift your priorities?
?
The passage says false calls do not endure. Examine your own spiritual practices: are they built on humble sincerity that will last, or on pride that will collapse? What is one habit you need to abandon or adopt to ensure your faith endures?

Ezekiel's Vine Prophecy and Its Fulfillment in Mecca
Sanusi interprets Ezekiel's vineyard prophecy as referring to Mecca and Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets Ezekiel's prophecy of the vine as a prophecy about Mecca and the coming of Muhammad.

Core Idea
Ezekiel's forgotten vine prophecy points directly to Muhammad's mission in Mecca.

Sanusi continues his proof of prophethood by turning to the Hebrew scriptures. In this passage, he cites the prophet Ezekiel's allegory of a vine that is uprooted and replaced by a new planting in the wilderness. Sanusi identifies this new planting with Mecca and, by implication, with the Prophet Muhammad. This lesson shows how Islamic scholars read earlier scriptures as pointing to the final prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the prophecy and Sanusi's interpretation sink in.
Notice the language: 'neglected, thirsty land' is key.
2
Identify the key elements
The prophecy has a vine (Israel), uprooting, new planting in the wilderness, fire from branches. Mark each element.
3
Understand Sanusi's interpretation
Sanusi says the 'neglected thirsty land' is Mecca because it is a desert and had no prophecy since Ishmael. The new planting is the coming of Muhammad.
This is a typological interpretation.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider how this prophecy fits into Sanusi's overall proof of Muhammad's prophethood. It uses previous scriptures to show foretelling.
This is a common method in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تبشير حزقيال عليه السلام ] وفي صحف حزقيال النبي يقولُ عن اللهِ عزَّ وجلَّ بعد ما ذكرَ معاصي بني إسرائيل وشبَّهَهم بكَرْمَةِ وقال : ( لم تلبث تلكَ الكَرْمَةُ أنْ قلِعَتْ بالسخطة ، ورُمِيَ بها على الأرضِ ، وأحرقَتِ السمائمُ ثمارها (۱) ، فعند ذلكَ غُرِسَ غرسُ في البدو ، وفي الأرض المهملة العطشى ، وخرجَتْ مِنْ أغصانِها الفاضلة نارٌ أكلَتْ تلكَ الكَرْمَةَ ، حتى لم يُوجَدْ فيها غصن قوي ولا قضيب ) (۲) فاعتبر هذا التصريح بهِ وبصفة بلدِهِ كلَّها ، وقوله : ( الأرض المهملة ، البدو ، العطشى ( ، وتلك صفاتُ مكَّةَ ؛ لأنَّها صحراء ، ولأنَّها كانَتْ مهملةً مِنَ النبوَّةِ مِنْ عهدِ إسماعيل عليه السلام .
Prophecy of Ezekiel, peace be upon him. And in the scriptures of the prophet Ezekiel, he says about Allah, Mighty and Majestic, after he mentioned the sins of the Children of Israel and likened them to a vine and said: 'That vine did not remain long; it was uprooted in anger and thrown to the ground, and the hot winds burned its fruits. Then at that time, a planting was planted in the wilderness, in the neglected, thirsty land, and from its excellent branches a fire came out and devoured that vine, so that no strong branch or twig was found in it.' So consider this clear statement about him and about the description of his entire land, and his saying: 'the neglected land, the wilderness, the thirsty,' and those are the characteristics of Mecca; because it is a desert, and because it was neglected from prophethood since the time of Ishmael, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage is a prophetic proof from the scriptures of Ezekiel. Sanusi quotes Ezekiel's allegory of a vine representing Israel, which is uprooted and burned. He then focuses on the new planting in the wilderness, on neglected thirsty land. Sanusi interprets this 'neglected thirsty land' as Mecca, which was without prophecy after Ishmael. The 'planting' is understood as the coming of Muhammad. The argument follows the author's pattern: cite the prophecy, then show its fulfillment in Muhammad.

Correction: Sanusi explicitly identifies the 'neglected thirsty land' with Mecca, a desert with no prophecy since Ishmael, pointing to Muhammad.

Daniel's Prophecy: The 30-Year Test for False Prophets
Sanusi cites Daniel's statement on false prophets' duration as proof for Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses Daniel's prophecy about the limited duration of false prophets as a proof for the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
A false prophet's call cannot exceed thirty years; Muhammad's call has lasted centuries.

Sanusi presents a striking proof from the scriptures of Prophet Daniel. When false prophets arise, their influence cannot last more than thirty years—a divine limit. Muhammad's call, by contrast, has endured for nearly nine hundred years and continues. This stark difference demonstrates that his prophethood is genuine.

Guided Path
1
Read Daniel's Prophecy
Read the Arabic quote from Daniel carefully. Note the claim: false prophets' call does not exceed thirty years.
The quote is introduced with 'وفي صحف دانيال النبي عليه السلام'.
2
Consider the Implication
Sanusi then applies this criterion to Muhammad. Understand that if Muhammad were false, his call would have ended long ago.
3
Reflect on the Time Gap
At the time of writing, Muhammad's call had lasted about 900 years. This far exceeds thirty years, so the test proves truth.
The number 900 is approximate and still growing.
4
Connect to Overall Proof
This is one of many proofs from previous scriptures that Sanusi uses. See how external prophecies confirm Muhammad's prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي صحف دانيال النبي عليه السلام وقد نعت الكذَّابينَ وقالَ : ) لا تمتد دعوتهم ، ولا يتمُّ قربانهم ، وأقسم الربُّ بساعده لا يظهرُ الباطل ولا يقومُ لمدَّعِ كاذب دعوة أكثرَ مِنْ ثلاثين سنة )(۳) فاعتبر من هذا الكلام عدم طول دعوة الكذابينَ ، وهذه دعوة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قائمةٌ ظاهرة قريباً مِنْ تسع مئة سنة ، وهي باقية إلى يوم القيامة .
And in the scriptures of Daniel the prophet, peace be upon him, when he described the liars and said: 'Their call will not extend, nor will their offering be completed, and the Lord has sworn by His arm that falsehood will not appear, nor will a false claimant have a call for more than thirty years.' So consider from this speech the non-prolongation of the call of liars, and this call of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is standing, apparent, for nearly nine hundred years, and it remains until the Day of Judgment.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage is another prophetic proof. Sanusi quotes Daniel's statement that false prophets' influence does not exceed thirty years. He then applies this criterion to Muhammad's call, which has lasted nearly nine hundred years at the time of writing, and continues. Therefore, Muhammad cannot be a false prophet; his long duration is a sign of truth.

Key Terms

الكذَّابين
دعوة
ثلاثين سنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Sanusi uses it as a maximum; the point is that Muhammad's far longer duration disproves falsehood.

Key Takeaway

?

Daniel's Dream of the Statue and Its Interpretation
Sanusi narrates Daniel's dream and its interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details of Daniel's dream of the statue and its interpretation as successive empires and the stone as an eternal kingdom.

Core Idea
In Daniel's dream, history's empires are symbolized by a statue, and the stone is the eternal kingdom of Islam.

This lesson presents the famous dream of King Nebuchadnezzar as interpreted by Daniel. The dream uses a statue of different materials to represent a sequence of world empires, culminating in a stone that destroys them all and grows to fill the earth. Understanding this prophecy helps us see how earlier scriptures pointed to the coming of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic passage describing the statue and the stone. Notice the materials: gold, silver, brass, iron, and clay.
The dream is vivid and symbolic.
2
Identify the interpretation
Daniel interprets each part of the statue: gold is Nebuchadnezzar, silver is his son, brass is the Romans, iron is the Persians, and clay is two weak nations ruled by women.
This shows the dream is about a succession of empires.
3
Focus on the stone
The stone that destroys the statue and becomes a great mountain is interpreted as 'the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom' that will come at the end of time.

وقال أيضاً دانيالُ النبيُّ وقد سألَهُ الملك بختنصرُ عن منامة رآها وطلب منه أن يخبره بها ثم بتفسيرها ، فقالَ : أيُّها الملكُ ؛ رأيت صنماً بارع الجمالِ ؛ أعلاهُ مِنْ ذهب ، ووسطهُ مِنْ فضةٍ ، وأسفلُهُ مِنْ نُحاس وساقاه من حديد ، ورجلاهُ مِنْ فَخَارٍ ، فبينما أنتَ تنظرُ إليهِ قد أعجبَكَ إِذْ نزلَ حجرٌ مِنَ السماءِ فضرب رأس الصنم ، فطحنه حتى اختلط ذهبُهُ وفضَّتُهُ ونُحاسُهُ وحديدُهُ وفَخَارُهُ ، ثم إِنَّ الحجر ربا وعظُمَ حتى ملأ الأرضَ كلَّها فقالَ لهُ بُختنصَّرُ : صدقت ، فأخبرني بتأويلها فقال له دانیال عليه السلام : أمَّا الصنم فأمم مختلفة في أوَّلِ الزمانِ وفي وسطه وآخرِهِ ؛ فالرأسُ مِنَ الذهب أنتَ أيُّها الملكُ ، والفضةُ ابنُكَ مِنْ بعدِكَ ، والنحاس الروم ، والحديد الفرسُ ، والفَخَارُ أمَّتانِ ضعیفتانِ تملكُهُما امرأتان باليمن والشام ، والحجرُ النازلُ مِنَ السماءِ دين نبي ومُلكُ أبدي يكونُ في آخرِ الزمانِ ، يغلبُ الأممَ كلَّها ، ثم يعظم حتى يملأ الأرض كلَّها كما ملأها ذلكَ الحجرُ (1), فانظر : هل كان نبي غير نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بُعِثَ إلى جميع الأمم ، وجعل جميعَ أجناسها على اختلاف أديانها واختلاف لغاتِها جنساً واحداً وعلى لغةٍ واحدةٍ ؟! إِذْ كلُّهم يقرؤونَ القرآنَ بلغةِ العرب ، ويدينون بدينٍ واحدٍ . وبالجملة : فنصوص الكتب الماضية في إثباتِ رسالة نبينا ومولانا محمدٍ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وبشاراتُ الأنبياء والأحبارِ به. لا تكاد
And Daniel the prophet also said, when King Nebuchadnezzar asked him about a dream he had seen and asked him to inform him of it and then its interpretation: 'O king, you saw a statue of striking beauty; its head was of gold, its middle of silver, its lower part of brass, its legs of iron, and its feet of clay. While you were looking at it, amazed, a stone descended from heaven and struck the head of the statue, grinding it until its gold, silver, brass, iron, and clay were mixed. Then the stone grew and became large until it filled the whole earth.' Nebuchadnezzar said: 'You have spoken truth, so tell me its interpretation.' Daniel, peace be upon him, said: 'As for the statue, it represents different nations in the beginning, middle, and end of time: the head of gold is you, O king; the silver is your son after you; the brass is the Romans; the iron is the Persians; the clay is two weak nations ruled by two women in Yemen and Syria. The stone that descended from heaven is the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom that will be at the end of time, overpowering all nations, then growing until it fills the whole earth just as that stone filled it.' So consider: was there any prophet other than our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, sent to all nations, making all their races—despite the differences in their religions and languages—one race with one language? For all of them read the Qur'an in the language of the Arabs and follow one religion. In short: the texts of the previous scriptures in establishing the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the tidings of the prophets and rabbis about him, are numerous.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage presents Daniel's famous dream of the statue made of different metals and the stone that destroys it. Sanusi recounts the dream and its interpretation as given by Daniel to Nebuchadnezzar: the statue representing successive empires, and the stone representing an eternal kingdom and religion that will fill the earth. Sanusi then applies this to Islam: Muhammad was sent to all nations, making them one community with one language (Arabic) for the Qur'an and one religion. He concludes by emphasizing the abundance of prophecies in prior scriptures about Muhammad.

بختنصر

حجر
مُلك أبدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The stone represents a political kingdom like the Roman Empire.
Correction: Daniel clearly says the stone is 'the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom' — it is a religious and spiritual kingdom that transcends earthly empires.

Checkpoint
According to Daniel's interpretation, what does the stone represent?
A) The Roman Empire
B) The Persian Empire
C) The religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom
D) The Babylonian kingdom

Key Takeaway
Daniel's dream of the statue foretells a succession of empires that are all destroyed by an eternal kingdom represented by a stone from heaven.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The stone from heaven shattered the magnificent statue of worldly empires. What 'statues' in your life—success, status, relationships, or ambitions—are you secretly trusting in instead of the eternal kingdom? Will you allow God's 'stone' to smash them today and surrender your heart fully to His reign?
?
Daniel said the stone is 'the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom.' Does your daily life demonstrate that you belong to an eternal kingdom, or are you living as if this world is all there is? What concrete change can you make this week to prioritize the eternal over the temporary?
?
You see the rise and fall of nations and leaders. The dream shows every human empire eventually crumbles. What if your own plans, even the good ones, are just 'clay feet'? Are you willing to let God replace your plans with His? What step can you take today to seek His kingdom first?

The Stone as the Eternal Kingdom of Muhammad
Sanusi applies Daniel's dream explicitly to Muhammad and Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi applies Daniel's dream to Muhammad, showing that the stone symbolizes the universal religion of Islam.

Core Idea
The stone in Daniel's dream is the religion of Muhammad, uniting all nations under one language and faith.

After recounting Daniel's interpretation, Sanusi asks a rhetorical question: Is there any prophet other than Muhammad who was sent to all nations and made them one community with one language? He then states that the previous scriptures are full of prophecies about Muhammad. This lesson explores how the stone in the dream points specifically to Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the rhetorical question
Read Sanusi's question: 'Was there any prophet other than our Prophet and Master Muhammad sent to all nations?' Think about the uniqueness of Muhammad's universal mission.
This question is the key application.
2
Understand the argument
Sanusi says that under Islam, all races become one race with one language (Arabic) for reading the Qur'an and one religion. This fulfills the stone filling the whole earth.
3
Note the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that the texts of previous scriptures contain many prophecies about Muhammad. This reinforces the truth of his prophethood.
The passage ends abruptly; likely continues.

Prophethood

Daniel's Dream Interpretation as Proof of Muhammad's Prophethood
Sanusi recounts Daniel's interpretation of the statue dream and applies it to Muhammad's prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the biblical story of Daniel interpreting Nebuchadnezzar's dream as a proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecy from previous scriptures confirms Muhammad's universal mission.

Sanusi employs a narrative from the Book of Daniel to demonstrate that the coming of Muhammad was foretold in earlier scriptures. In this passage, he recounts Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream of a statue, identifying the stone that crushes the statue as the eternal religious kingdom of Islam. The rhetorical question that follows emphasizes that only Muhammad's prophethood united all nations under one language and one religion, fulfilling the prophecy. This lesson explores how Sanusi uses this story as a proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage along with its translation. Notice the detailed description of the dream and its interpretation.
The passage is a single continuous narrative.
2
Identify the prophecy and its fulfillment
Focus on Daniel's interpretation: the stone represents a prophet's religion and an eternal kingdom. Sanusi then asks whether any other prophet brought all nations into one language and religion.
This is the core argument: the dream predicts Muhammad's mission.
3
Understand the rhetorical question
Sanusi ends with a rhetorical question highlighting the uniqueness of Muhammad: he was sent to all nations and made them one community with Arabic as the language of the Quran.
This shows the universal nature of Islam as the fulfillment of the prophecy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أيضاً دانيالُ النبيُّ وقد سألَهُ الملك بختنصرُ عن منامة رآها وطلب منه أن يخبره بها ثم بتفسيرها ، فقالَ : أيُّها الملكُ ؛ رأيت صنماً بارع الجمالِ ؛ أعلاهُ مِنْ ذهب ، ووسطهُ مِنْ فضةٍ ، وأسفلُهُ مِنْ نُحاس وساقاه من حديد ، ورجلاهُ مِنْ فَخَارٍ ، فبينما أنتَ تنظرُ إليهِ قد أعجبَكَ إِذْ نزلَ حجرٌ مِنَ السماءِ فضرب رأس الصنم ، فطحنه حتى اختلط ذهبُهُ وفضَّتُهُ ونُحاسُهُ وحديدُهُ وفَخَارُهُ ، ثم إِنَّ الحجر ربا وعظُمَ حتى ملأ الأرضَ كلَّها فقالَ لهُ بُختنصَّرُ : صدقت ، فأخبرني بتأويلها فقال له دانیال عليه السلام : أمَّا الصنم فأمم مختلفة في أوَّلِ الزمانِ وفي وسطه وآخرِهِ ؛ فالرأسُ مِنَ الذهب أنتَ أيُّها الملكُ ، والفضةُ ابنُكَ مِنْ بعدِكَ ، والنحاس الروم ، والحديد الفرسُ ، والفَخَارُ أمَّتانِ ضعیفتانِ تملكُهُما امرأتان باليمن والشام ، والحجرُ النازلُ مِنَ السماءِ دين نبي ومُلكُ أبدي يكونُ في آخرِ الزمانِ ، يغلبُ الأممَ كلَّها ، ثم يعظم حتى يملأ الأرض كلَّها كما ملأها ذلكَ الحجرُ (1), فانظر : هل كان نبي غير نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بُعِثَ إلى جميع الأمم ، وجعل جميعَ أجناسها على اختلاف أديانها واختلاف لغاتِها جنساً واحداً وعلى لغةٍ واحدةٍ ؟! إِذْ كلُّهم يقرؤونَ القرآنَ بلغةِ العرب ، ويدينون بدينٍ واحدٍ • وبالجملة : فنصوص الكتب الماضية في إثباتِ رسالة نبينا ومولانا محمدٍ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وبشاراتُ الأنبياء والأحبارِ بهِ. لا تكاد تنحصرُ ، ويكفي هذا الذي أشرنا إليه منها في هذا المختصر
And Daniel the prophet also said, when King Nebuchadnezzar asked him about a dream he saw and asked him to tell it to him and then its interpretation, he said: 'O king, I saw a statue of perfect beauty; its top was of gold, its middle of silver, its lower part of brass, its legs of iron, and its feet of clay. While you were looking at it, admiring it, behold, a stone fell from heaven and struck the head of the statue, grinding it until its gold, silver, brass, iron, and clay mixed together; then the stone grew and became great until it filled all the earth.' Nebuchadnezzar said to him: 'You have spoken truth, so tell me its interpretation.' Daniel, peace be upon him, said: 'As for the statue, it is different nations in the beginning of time, its middle, and its end. The head of gold is you, O king; the silver is your son after you; the brass is the Romans; the iron is the Persians; the clay is two weak nations ruled by two women in Yemen and Syria; and the stone descending from heaven is the religion of a prophet and an eternal kingdom at the end of time; it will overcome all nations, then grow until it fills all the earth just as that stone filled it.' So consider: was there a prophet other than our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, sent to all nations, making all their races, despite the differences of their religions and differences of their languages, into one race and one language? For they all recite the Quran in the language of the Arabs and adhere to one religion. In summary: the texts of the previous scriptures concerning the proof of the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the glad tidings of the prophets and rabbis concerning him, are nearly limitless, and what we have indicated of them in this abridgment suffices.
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the prophethood of Muhammad using a biblical narrative. Sanusi recounts the interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream by the prophet Daniel, as found in the Book of Daniel. The dream features a statue made of different metals representing successive empires (Babylon, Medo-Persia, Greece, Rome), and a stone cut without hands that crushes the statue and becomes a mountain filling the earth. Sanusi applies this to Muhammad, arguing that the stone represents an eternal religious kingdom that overcomes all others. He then asks rhetorically whether any prophet other than Muhammad was sent to all nations and made them one community with one language (Arabic) and one religion (Islam). Thus, the fulfillment of this dream in Muhammad's universal mission is a proof from previous scriptures. Sanusi concludes that such proofs are abundant and the example given is sufficient for this summary.

دانيال
بختنصر
الصنم
العرب
لغة العرب

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Sanusi uses Daniel's interpretation of Nebuchadnezzar's dream to demonstrate that Muhammad's universal prophethood was foretold in previous scriptures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi uses a dream from 2,500 years ago as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood. When you read this, do you truly feel the weight of that connection, or does it remain a distant intellectual fact? What would change in your daily life if you fully internalized that your Prophet was foretold by every previous prophet?
?
Consider: the stone grew until it filled the earth. Muhammad's message has spread across the globe. Are you actively contributing to that growth in your own sphere, or are you content to let others carry the stone? What specific step will you take this week to make Islam more present in your community?
?
The prophecy says the stone 'grinds' all previous kingdoms into dust. What personal 'kingdoms'—pride, worldly ambitions, attachments—are you still clinging to that have not been crushed by the truth of Muhammad's message? Will you let the stone break them today?

The Name Muhammad Before Islam
Sanusi lists seven individuals named Muhammad before the Prophet's birth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the name Muhammad was not entirely unknown before the Prophet's birth, and you will be able to identify the seven individuals named Muhammad as enumerated by Sanusi.

Core Idea
The name Muhammad was rare but known before the Prophet's birth.

Sanusi addresses a potential objection that the name Muhammad was invented or unknown before Islam. He provides a list of seven individuals who bore this name shortly before the Prophet's birth. This passage not only refutes that objection but also demonstrates the divine wisdom in choosing a name that was rare yet recognized.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Sanusi begins with 'except a few people' which implies that the name was uncommon.
Pay attention to the vowel markings in the Arabic; they are provided to avoid mispronunciation.
2
Identify the seven names
Locate each of the seven individuals. They are listed with their full names and sometimes tribal affiliations.
Write down the names in order to memorize them.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why would Sanusi list these names? What does this list tell us about the name Muhammad before Islam?
Consider that the list shows the name existed, but its rarity underscores its special association with the Prophet.

قولُهُ : ( إلا أُناساً قليلين تسموا قريباً مِنْ مولده باسمه ( عددهم سبعة : محمد بن مسلمة الأنصاري ، ومحمدُ بنُ أُحَيْحَةَ بنِ الجُلاح - بضم الهمزة وحاءين مهملتين مفتوحتين بينهما يا ساكنة ، والجُلاحُ : بضم الجيم ولام مخففة وآخرُهُ حاء مهملة - ومحمد بن براء البكري بتخفيف الراء ، ومحمد بن سفيانَ بنِ مجاشع ، ومحمدُ بنُ حُمْرانَ الجُعفيُّ ، ومحمدُ بنُ خزاعة السلمي ، ومحمدُ بنُ اليَحْمدي بفتح الياء وضم الميم وفتحها
His statement: 'Except a few people who were named with his name shortly before his birth; they number seven: Muhammad ibn Maslamah al-Ansari, Muhammad ibn Uhayhah ibn al-Julah (with dammah on the hamzah and two open ha' with a sukun ya between them, and al-Julah with dammah on the jim and lightened lam and ending with a silent ha), Muhammad ibn Bara' al-Bakri with lightened ra', Muhammad ibn Sufyan ibn Mujashi', Muhammad ibn Humran al-Ju'fi, Muhammad ibn Khuzarah al-Sulami, and Muhammad ibn al-Yahmadi with fatha on the ya and dammah on the mim and fatha on it.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of seven individuals who were named Muhammad shortly before the birth of the Prophet. Sanusi is likely responding to an objection that the name Muhammad was unknown before Islam. He provides a list with careful vocalization to avoid misreading. The list includes: Muhammad ibn Maslamah al-Ansari, Muhammad ibn Uhayhah ibn al-Julah, Muhammad ibn Bara' al-Bakri, Muhammad ibn Sufyan ibn Mujashi', Muhammad ibn Humran al-Ju'fi, Muhammad ibn Khuzarah al-Sulami, and Muhammad ibn al-Yahmadi. This shows that the name was used, but only by a few, implying that it was not common and thus its association with the Prophet was divinely guided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the name Muhammad was entirely unknown before Islam and was invented by the Prophet's parents.
Correction: This passage shows that the name existed before the Prophet's birth, though it was rare. The list of seven individuals demonstrates its prior usage.

Checkpoint
How many people were named Muhammad shortly before the Prophet's birth according to this passage?
A) Five
B) Seven
C) Ten
D) Three

Key Takeaway
The name Muhammad was known and used by seven individuals before the Prophet's birth, confirming that the name was not a post-Islamic invention.

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
The Certainty of Prophethood: Necessary Knowledge and Obligatory Faith
Sanusi concludes the prophethood section, stating the result of cumulative proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how cumulative evidence from prophethood proofs leads to necessary knowledge of Muhammad's truthfulness and why this obligates belief in all details of the faith.

Core Idea
Cumulative proofs yield certain knowledge that demands full acceptance.

Sanusi concludes his discussion on prophethood by tying together all the previous evidence. He explains that when you are granted success in understanding all the proofs, you attain necessary knowledge—immediate certainty—that Muhammad's message is true. This certainty then imposes the duty to believe in everything the Prophet brought, both in general and in every specific teaching, such as the afterlife and the grave's punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Notice that it is a conclusion that summarizes the result of the entire prophethood section.
The heading has a typo: 'النيبنيات' should be 'النبويات' or 'النبوات'.
2
Understand 'necessary knowledge'
Sanusi says 'حصل لكَ العلم ضرورةً' meaning necessary knowledge. This is immediate, certain knowledge, not speculative. Reflect on how cumulative evidence produces such certainty.
3
Identify the obligation and the examples
The passage states that faith becomes obligatory in everything the Prophet brought, in general and in detail. List the examples Sanusi provides (e.g., the Gathering, the Path, etc.) and consider why these specific beliefs are mentioned.
These examples are from the unseen (sam'iyyat) that must be accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام على النيبنيات فإذا وُفِّقْتَ لعلم هذا كله حصل لكَ العلم ضرورةً بصدق رسالة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فوجبَ الإيمانُ بهِ في كلِّ ما جاءَ بِهِ عَنِ اللَّهِ سبحانَهُ جملةً وتفصيلاً ؛ كالحشر والنشر ، والصراطِ والميزان ، والجنة والنار ، وعذاب القبر وسؤالِهِ
Discussion on prophethood: For if you are granted success in knowing all of this, necessary knowledge of the truthfulness of the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is attained for you. Then faith becomes obligatory in everything he brought from Allah, Exalted is He, in general and in detail, such as the Gathering and the Spreading [of scrolls], the Path and the Balance, Paradise and the Fire, the punishment of the grave and its questioning.
Source pages p. 611

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion to the section on prophethood. Sanusi states that if one is granted success in understanding the evidence presented (including the Daniel prophecy and other proofs from previous scriptures), one will attain necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) of the truthfulness of Muhammad's message. This knowledge is not merely inferential but immediate and certain. Once this knowledge is attained, it becomes obligatory to believe in everything the Prophet brought from Allah, both in general (that he is truthful) and in detail (specific beliefs). Sanusi lists examples of detailed beliefs: the Resurrection, the Gathering, the Spreading of scrolls, the Path (صراط), the Balance (ميزان), Paradise, Hell, and the punishment and questioning in the grave. Thus, the cumulative evidence from previous scriptures leads to certain faith that compels acceptance of all Islamic teachings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that necessary knowledge is attained from a single proof, but Sanusi implies it comes from cumulative evidence ('هذا كله').
Correction: Necessary knowledge in this context results from considering the entirety of the prophethood evidence, not any single piece alone.

Checkpoint
What type of knowledge is attained according to Sanusi when one considers all the evidence?
A) Speculative knowledge
B) Necessary knowledge (علم ضروري)
C) Probable knowledge
D) Imitative knowledge

Key Takeaway
Cumulative evidence from prophethood proofs yields necessary knowledge that Muhammad is truthful, obligating belief in all Islamic teachings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading that cumulative evidence leads to necessary knowledge of Muhammad's truthfulness, ask yourself: Do I possess that necessary knowledge, or do I still harbor doubts? What evidence from this lesson stands between me and complete certainty?
?
You are commanded to believe in everything the Prophet brought, in general and in detail. Is there any specific belief—like the punishment of the grave or the scales—that you have neglected or allowed yourself to question? If so, what will you do today to rectify that?
?
If you truly accept that faith is obligatory in all details, then what is one teaching of the Prophet that you find difficult to implement in your daily life? What step will you take this week to submit to it fully?
